  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_116cb5f6-5a3a-4dd2-802d-fc864cab290e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer12871769460984289060"><i>In a galaxy powered by the current, everyone has a gift.</i><br/><br/>Cyra is the sister of the brutal tyrant who rules the Shotet people.   <span id="freeText12871769460984289060" style="display:none"><i>In a galaxy powered by the current, everyone has a gift.</i><br /><br />Cyra is the sister of the brutal tyrant who rules the Shotet people. Cyra’s currentgift gives her pain and power—something her brother exploits, using her to torture his enemies. But Cyra is much more than just a blade in her brother’s hand: she is resilient, quick on her feet, and smarter than he knows.<br /><br />Akos is the son of a farmer and an oracle from the frozen nation-planet of Thuvhe. Protected by his unusual currentgift, Akos is generous in spirit, and his loyalty to his family is limitless. Once Akos and his brother are captured by enemy Shotet soldiers, Akos is desperate to get his brother out alive—no matter what the cost.<br /><br />Then Akos is thrust into Cyra's world, and the enmity between their countries and families seems insurmountable. Will they help each other to survive, or will they destroy one another?<br /><br /><i>Carve the Mark</i> is Veronica Roth's stunning portrayal of the power of friendship—and love—in a galaxy filled with unexpected gifts.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1403417152?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2016</a>

        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1403417152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9262553913027347045">1 1/2 stars. Just.... soooo sloooowwww.<br/><br/>Let's be honest, I actually liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_' title='Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Divergent</a> for what it was - a fast-paced, exciting YA adventure that demanded very little of me. Sure, a lot of the world made absolutely no sense, and I still find that whole "I'm Dauntless so I jump off moving trains" thing so ridiculously laughable, but I found it really entertaining. In this book, though, <b>I spent the majority of it wondering where the actual plot was</b>.<br/><br/>It's set in space, and I've heard other reviewers tal</span>
  <span id="freeText9262553913027347045" style="display:none">1 1/2 stars. Just.... soooo sloooowwww.<br /><br />Let's be honest, I actually liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a> for what it was - a fast-paced, exciting YA adventure that demanded very little of me. Sure, a lot of the world made absolutely no sense, and I still find that whole "I'm Dauntless so I jump off moving trains" thing so ridiculously laughable, but I found it really entertaining. In this book, though, <b>I spent the majority of it wondering where the actual plot was</b>.<br /><br />It's set in space, and I've heard other reviewers talking positively about how it doesn't <i>feel</i> like it's in space, so maybe that will also seem like a positive for you, but I felt like this story could have been set literally anywhere. The world-building was lacking and the space aspect left undeveloped. Why even bother setting it in space if you're not going to make the most of that? Though I guess there's a definite possibility that the second book will reveal that the characters have actually been in Brooklyn all along, tripping on acid. So, there's that.<br /><br />The story is set on a distant planet where people develop unique powers known as currentgifts, bestowed by a magical current that runs through the galaxy. Most people find their gifts useful, but to some people - like Akos and Cyra - the gifts can be a burden, and a means by which others can use them for their own gains. Cyra's violent and evil brother is the ruler of the Shotet and he uses Cyra's power - the power to deliver intense pain - to further his plans and torture his enemies. <br /><br />Akos, on the other hand, is one of the gentle Thuvhe people. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30117284.Carve_the_Mark__Carve_the_Mark___1_" title="Carve the Mark (Carve the Mark, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Carve the Mark</a> opens with Shotet soldiers murdering Akos's father and capturing him and his younger brother. What happens next is a very long bit of filler about Akos's time in the Shotet soldier camp, honing his fighting skills and chatting with Cyra about their countries, their powers, or just their favourite colours. I was more than halfway through and wondering when something was going to happen.<br /><br /><b>It wasn't compelling enough</b>. The characters themselves were not interesting enough. If I wasn't wary of the backlash I would get from writing a DNF review, I would have put it aside. The action occasionally picks up but it's not the start of a change of pace; it quickly dies down again. I felt like something happened once every hundred pages.<br /><br />And it's not so easy to mask the simplicity, the lack of creativity, in Roth's latest work. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a> had just enough quirks to make it stand out against the odds - the use of factions an exciting reminder of Hogwarts' houses for old Potterheads, and a new personality quiz for younger readers. Even those feeling underwhelmed were quick to take a faction quiz to see where they fell (Candor - thanks for asking!). <br /><br />What does <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30117284.Carve_the_Mark__Carve_the_Mark___1_" title="Carve the Mark (Carve the Mark, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Carve the Mark</a> have to make it stand out? I honestly don't have an answer.<br /><br />The world is very simplistic. The Xmen-like powers are nothing we haven't seen before hundreds of times. The politics are uninteresting and the villain is mindlessly evil without any depth or development. <br /><br />I said in a status update that there had been some confusion over the physical descriptions of the characters - that the violent savages are actually described as "so pale he looked almost like a corpse" and the pacifist Thuvhe people have "light brown skin" and "dense, curly hair" - but the reality is only marginally better than the rumours. Having a violently savage race vs. a gentle race without it being adequately addressed is arguably always problematic; it arguably always has troubling real-world connotations. And, even if you disagree with that assessment, at best it's just plain lazy.<br /><br />A hard slog and utterly forgettable.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9262553913027347045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1631497161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1631497161" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1631497161?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008159481" href="/book/show/30233110-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=free-from-work">free-from-work</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1631497161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10919149128505995119"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best YA fantasy! what will happen?</b><br/><br/>i'm going to review this without giving too much away, which seems to be the publisher's desire, since this is the first time i have ever gotten an arc that had this<br/><br/><a href='http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley003/IMG_8396_zpsfxkgc6pr.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480202168i/21284148._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo IMG_8396_zpsfxkgc6pr.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>across every single page. <br/><br/>text blurred so no one yells at me. <br/><br/>DON'T YELL AT ME!<br/><br/>i am someone who liked the divergent trilogy. i even sort of liked those four stories: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18126198.Four_A_Divergent_Story_Collection__Divergent___0_1___0_4_' title='Four A Divergent Story Collection (Divergent, #0.1 - 0.4) by Veronica Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Four: A Divergent Story Collection</a>. <br/><br/>but i am SO SO pleased that roth has <i>diverged</i> (h</span>
  <span id="freeText10919149128505995119" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best YA fantasy! what will happen?</b><br><br>i'm going to review this without giving too much away, which seems to be the publisher's desire, since this is the first time i have ever gotten an arc that had this<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley003/IMG_8396_zpsfxkgc6pr.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480202168i/21284148._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_8396_zpsfxkgc6pr.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>across every single page. <br><br>text blurred so no one yells at me. <br><br>DON'T YELL AT ME!<br><br>i am someone who liked the divergent trilogy. i even sort of liked those four stories: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18126198.Four_A_Divergent_Story_Collection__Divergent___0_1___0_4_" title="Four A Divergent Story Collection (Divergent, #0.1 - 0.4) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Four: A Divergent Story Collection</a>. <br><br>but i am SO SO pleased that roth has <i>diverged</i> (ho-HO!) from that path and gone off in a whole new direction with this book (which is apparently the first part of a duology). i do love an author with more than one idea in their head.<br><br>in a lot of ways, this book is like saga<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1428350405l/15704307.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>it's got that same romeo and juliet in spaaaaaaace thing going on, where two people on opposite sides of a long and deeply-rooted cultural animosity develop special feelings for each other after one of them is basically the prisoner of the other. <br><br><a href="http://s1260.photobucket.com/user/Henchman4Hire3/media/Saga803_zpsd226e817.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480202480i/21284155._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo Saga803_zpsd226e817.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>no wings, no horns, and no teevee-headed people, but the two crazy kids in this book do have some unusual abilities in the form of currentgifts.<br><br>currentgifts. <br>currentgifts.<br>currentgifts.<br>currentgifts.<br><br>i still think this is a dumb word, but it's a little less dumb than i expected going into it. "current" does not mean a "now" gift, which is how i interpreted it from the synopsis, but rather to a gift from a magical current that runs through the galaxy, doling out special abilities to people. some of these abilities are useful, and some are more like burdens than gifts. think x-men. in spaaaaaaaace.<br><br>i am not usually a fan of space-based novels, and i'm even less enthusiastic about the romantic parts of books, especially in YA. however, i most certainly enjoyed this book. the fact that it is set in space is easy to forget, which sounds like a criticism, but worked out well for me. it's <i>otherworldly</i>, but it's not full of people floating about in spacesuits or going through wormholes or making me feel inadequate in my understanding of, you know, <i>science</i>. <br><br>the romance is what it is - it's certainly handled better than the romance in other books i have read (including divergent, now that i think about it). it unfolds slowly, it isn't too sappy, and it is grounded in circumstances that seem likely to inspire feelings of "you and me against the world;" where two characters who are treated as "other" by most people cleave to each other in their otherness and feelings develop in a way that makes sense. <br><br>although maybe not to them:<br><br><i>"You make no sense to me," she said.</i><br><br>and happily - cyra is not tris recast in spaaaaaaaace.<br><br>there are the superficial physical differences - cyra has darker skin, is much taller and … sturdier than tris, and by the end of the book, something happens that alters her appearance in a way that i personally think is SO FREAKING COOL, and also ghastly. but more importantly, her personality is not just warming up the tris leftovers. they are both proactive and badass with the fighting skills without getting too sentimental when violence needs doing, but cyra has had a much harder path dealt to her than tris, and it has toughened her worldview, giving her more depth and darkness than tris ever had. <br><br><i>Pity, I knew, was just disrespect wrapped in kindness.</i><br><br>i will confess, it took me some time to get into this one. it may have been my headspace at the time of reading, or it may truly have been a slow starter. <i>divergent</i> grabbed me from the get-go, and i had expected this would be a typically fast YA read for me, but i didn't start really digging it until i was about a third of the way through. some of the drag of it is indeed the names and sillywords, and some of it just doesn't make sense, but a lot of the divergent world didn't make a lick of sense, and it didn't stop it from being entertaining. if books had to make sense, christianity never would have caught on.<br><br>oh, and the title?<br><br>-<i>"Carve the mark," I said, my throat tight.</i><br><br>and<br><br>-<i>"Carve the mark," he said. He was so hoarse the words almost didn't come out.</i><br><br>what does it mean? why does it make throats tight and words hoarse? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480380684ra/21303115.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>blur blur blur - you'll have to wait for that.<br><br>***********************************************<br><br>i'm a little surprised by some of the negative reviews, 'cuz i liked it. are my critical faculties rusty? i'll review it soon and you can tell me i'm wrong. that's how this "goodreads" thing works, right? <br><br>***********************************************<br>OOH, i got my hands on an ARC! now i can enjoy many silly words and names and i hope it's fun!<br><br>i will dive in SOON!<br><br>***********************************************<br>i can't even make it through that synopsis without 1) getting bored and 2) activating my "fantasy genre silly-name" shield, but as one of the few people who <i>did</i> like the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18710190.Allegiant__Divergent___3_" title="Allegiant (Divergent, #3) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Allegiant</a> ended (or at least didn't have a problem with the thing most people hated it for), i gotta say i'm looking forward to this. bring it on, silly names and all!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

<div id="review_1866148973" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1866148973" />
    <a title="Meg (fairy.bookmother)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/774907-meg-fairy-bookmother"><img alt="Meg (fairy.bookmother)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593706410p2/774907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meg (fairy.bookmother)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meg (fairy.bookmother)" href="/user/show/774907-meg-fairy-bookmother">Meg (fairy.bookmother)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/774907-meg-fairy-bookmother?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1866148973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8916257155199842918">So, I should preface this with a few key points. I work for a bookstore and received an ARC of this book through my job. All opinions are my own. This review is not an attack on the author, the publisher, or anyone else. I am also white, and I am aware this affects my position to call something out as racist. I find that it's helpful to raise awareness of problematic representation in the media we consume.<br/><br/>In regards to advance copies being sent out to reviewers, I've noticed in a lot of Goodread</span>
  <span id="freeText8916257155199842918" style="display:none">So, I should preface this with a few key points. I work for a bookstore and received an ARC of this book through my job. All opinions are my own. This review is not an attack on the author, the publisher, or anyone else. I am also white, and I am aware this affects my position to call something out as racist. I find that it's helpful to raise awareness of problematic representation in the media we consume.<br /><br />In regards to advance copies being sent out to reviewers, I've noticed in a lot of Goodreads reviews that the bloggers state either at the beginning or the end of their review that HarperTeen (HT from here on out) <b>
  <i>sponsored</i>
</b> these reviews. Further research led me to discovering that HT <i>paid</i> this set of bloggers to review <i>Carve the Mark</i>. This behavior from a publisher is unsettling. Generally speaking, if one is going to be paid for reviewing something, one will not review the thing unfavorably (and if one reviews unfavorably, that reviewer runs the risk of tarnishing the relationship with said publisher). This behavior by the publisher is akin to self-published authors paying readers to post positive reviews of the work in order to boost sales. That's what I feel like HT is doing. Perhaps HT was aware of the problematic material in the book and decided to garner a set of positive reviews to boost sales before the book's official release. I feel as if that money could have been better used to assist Roth in adjusting some of the problematic ideas presented in the book.<br /><br />I stopped reading at page 66. I was simultaneously bored and unsettled by the book and set it aside. This being said, I do not know how the book ends or develops, and I honestly don't care. Here are the main things I found problematic within those first 66 pages:<br /><br />1. The Thuve and the Shotet. The Thuve are presented as a lighter skinned race who are passive. Akos, one of the main characters, views the Shotet as a brutal and fierce race of people (the Shotet killed Akos's grandmother). The first time the readers are introduced to the Shotet, the Shotet arrive to Akos's family farm and brutally murder his father.<br /><br />2. The Shotet language is described as harsh and gutteral by Akos compared to his own softer sounding language (who discovers he has the ability to speak other languages without prior conscious knowledge of them). This view of languages is similar to the comparisons of the "music" of Romance (white) languages (French, Italian, Spanish) to the "harsh, guttural" (black) languages of the African continent.<br /><br />3. While the Shotet are described has having varying tones of skin, Cyra's mother is described as having hair curly enough for fingers to be trapped in the curls while Cyra's is not as curly as that. Um. Okay.<br /><br />4. Cyra's brother Ryz forcibly trades one of his memories for one of Cyra's. Cyra obviously struggles against it and can't fight it, and you know what? That's rape. Forcing someone to take something mentally (and inevitably physically) is an act of rape. Cyra was raped by her own brother. As a result of that rape, Cyra's power manifests itself as pain. Literally. Pain. By page 66, Cyra cannot touch other people without feeling pain, and other people cannot touch her without feeling pain.<br /><br />5. Later, Cyra's mother asks the doctor "You're saying this gift is my daughter's fault? That she wants to be this way?" And the doctor (male) says, "Cyra, the gift comes from you. If you change, the gift will, too." So a man is telling a woman that her rape and her pain from that rape is her own fault and that she can change it at will. Yep. That's a blatant reinforcement of rape culture.<br /><br />6. The religion of the Shotet draws heavily from Islamic ideology. Some of the religious leaders are called clerics, and some of the practices reinforce the negative views the West has on Muslim culture. We need to move past these harmful stereotypes.<br /><br />7. While I enjoyed the Divergent trilogy well enough for what it is (even if it's a blatant knockoff of The Hunger Games and Harry Potter, it is also somewhat original in its ending), <i>Carve the Mark</i> is a lazy reimagining of the Star Wars and X-Men universes. It tries to be unique and diverse, but the glaring insensitivity within the first sixty pages result in its failing.<br /><br />I was excited for this because there aren't too many science fiction novels lately for the YA audience. However, the problems in the novel fail its readers by relying on outdated, racist tropes that should be a thing of the past in 2017. Science fiction is about creating new worlds, exploring new ideas, and finding some kernel of society to examine. <i>Carve the Mark</i> does none of this. Instead of drawing on redundant, harmful tropes, science fiction should offer the author and the readers the ability to create something new, to flip tropes and reinvent them. It seems as if the editors failed to notice or didn't care, knowing that they'd have a cash-grab with the popular name attached; or it seems as if Roth is privileged enough to be unaware of the damage she has caused with these themes. Maybe it's a combination of both.<br /><br />After the roller coaster of the last several years with the Black Lives Matter movement, the systematic oppression of Muslims, and the discussions I have had and read, I'm finding myself more and more sensitive to the plights of those who are oppressed. I want to give those people a voice rather than reinforce harmful views. Instead of purchasing or reading this, I recommend finding, like many others have suggested, an own voices/diverse work. My personal recommendation is N.K. Jemisin's <i>The Fifth Season.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8916257155199842918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1834915407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834915407" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834915407?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30133224-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=trees-died-for-this-crap">trees-died-for-this-crap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=1star">1star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=abn-readalongs">abn-readalongs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2017">read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834915407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15279458785036085318">Oh dear!! Where do I start?????<br/><br/>Racial stereotyping and questionable use of certain imagery.<br/>Ill advised plot lines that reinforce rape culture rather than expose it as negative<br/>Unflagged trigger warnings.<br/>And a romanticised depiction of chronic pain (something that is very personal to me).<br/><br/><br/>But let's begin with the writing. Wow talk about dull! The first half of this book was so incredibly tedious. The pace, the plotting, the world building (what world building?!?!)... It just dragged. It felt uninsp</span>
  <span id="freeText15279458785036085318" style="display:none">Oh dear!! Where do I start?????<br /><br />Racial stereotyping and questionable use of certain imagery.<br />Ill advised plot lines that reinforce rape culture rather than expose it as negative<br />Unflagged trigger warnings.<br />And a romanticised depiction of chronic pain (something that is very personal to me).<br /><br /><br />But let's begin with the writing. Wow talk about dull! The first half of this book was so incredibly tedious. The pace, the plotting, the world building (what world building?!?!)... It just dragged. It felt uninspired, insipid, unimaginative, take your pick! Was this book set in space??? It didn't feel like that to me. One of the things that I really didn't like with regards to the writing was the format of switching points of view. It just did not work because it was so poorly executed. It seemed much too haphazard and really hindered the flow of the narrative. <br /><br /><br />So the basic set up is there are two races of people sharing some planet. They hate each other because *reasons* and hatred &amp; drama ensue. <br /><br /><br />Okay. <b>Controversy number one: Racist undertones </b><br />Many people have been incredibly offended by the depiction of the races in this book saying that it reinforces negative stereotypes within our society. There's a seemingly more civilised race versus a more savage one. Personally I found that there was enough nuance with regard to the diversity of the descriptions of the physical appearances of the two races, BUT, I think this may have been due to my prior knowledge of this controversy because I was actively reading looking for the differences. If you step back from the book, the overall impression of the two races is not so clear. And there were also worrying descriptors used to ascribe differences between characters, e.g. a reference to curly hair kinky enough to capture a finger which is reminiscent of the pencil test used during apartheid times in South Africa to ascertain skin colour. An inadvertent unconscious similarity??? At any rate, I think that conceptually this was a problematic idea. Because division of race, even in a fantastical setting, is going to cause issues within our own reality. It <b>is </b>going to offend. And surely that isn't the way forward? Basically at times I felt the book was not as carefully researched as it should have been and therefore did not provide a well thought out and sensitively structured system of beliefs for the people in the story. <br /><br /><br /><b>Trigger Warning Self Harm</b> At this point I would like to draw your attention to some ritualistic behaviours the Shotet people do regarding marking their bodies. In particular during chapter 13 there is a very detailed description of something that could be incredibly triggering to anyone who has issues regarding self-harm. While I personally am okay with the theory behind this behaviour I strongly feel that there should be a warning on the back cover of this book with regards to this behaviour. When are authors and publishers going to take some responsibility for the possible detrimental effects of the content of their published works??? <br /><br /><br />Back to the story:<br />The three main characters in this book are:<br />Cyra, a Shotet girl who experiences chronic pain. <br />Her power hungry, villainous brother Ryzek.<br />And then there is Akos, a Thuvhesit boy fated to serve his Shotet enemy. <br /><br /><br />Let's start with Akos.... I've pretty much nothing to say about him. He was about as interesting as a piece of cardboard. Zero personality. One dimensional. Boring...move on!!!<br /><br /><br />Ryzek, the big bad. Likes to rape minds and steal memories. He could have been a quite chilling character but his portrayal descended into pantomime theatrics and a sensitive subject such as forcibly taking what you want and thereby violation of another person was very badly handled. <br /><br /><b>Next controversy: Rape Culture</b><br />So Ryzek rapes Cyra's mind thus causing the early onset of her <i>'currentgift' </i>which leaves her experiencing chronic pain for which she is ultimately told is her fault because she feels she deserves this pain... That bother anyone else??? Reinforce the idea of victim shaming/blaming???<br /><br /><br />And finally, there is Cyra. She's an interesting character. It's a bold move to attempt to write a character suffering from chronic pain... But was it a move that paid off??? <br />Well with regards to the storyline yes!<br />With regards to upsetting and offending sufferers of chronic pain then it's a big no. <br /><br /><br /><b>Chronic pain controversy</b><br />So here's a little information about me. <br />Many of my Goodreads friends will know that from time to time I have mentioned that I suffer from multiple chronic illnesses. (Yes multiple.) And one of those illnesses in particular causes great physical pain. It causes more pain than I could ever possibly explain to you. My chronic pain took hold of my life when I was still a child almost 25 years ago. So I think that living with chronic pain for the best part of a quarter of a century qualifies me to discuss it. <br /><br /><br />My first problem with Cyra's chronic pain is the terminology used. It is frequently described as a <i>'currentgift'. </i>In the glossary a <i>currentgift </i>is explained as follows: <i>thought to be a result of the current flowing through a person, currentgifts are abilities, unique to each person, that develop during puberty. They are not always benevolent</i>.<br />Isn't that last line about this currentgift not always being benevolent great??? As if it somehow excuses you from the offensive terminology of calling the suffering of the main character a 'gift'.<br /><br /><br />Here's a tip for you. Do not ever call chronic pain a gift. Even if it's in a slightly made-up word that you feel the need to explain in the back of your book. <br />What really annoyed me in this instance is how Cyra referred to her pain as a gift. I could accept anyone else in the book referring to it as such and put it down to their ignorance and then possibly have Cyra show why it should not be called such a thing... But she FREQUENTLY called it a gift without any hint of irony, derision or sense of injustice!!! Only once did she disagree, but then, instead of referring to the pain in some other manner, she continued on with this gift terminology. My pain is not, and will never be a gift. I will always experience pain. There is no out. And I am <b>incredibly offended</b> by even remotely suggesting that it could possibly be construed as a gift. Where is my gift receipt please because I'm sending this unwanted gift back!!! <br /><br />Also, my chronic pain is not an <i>ability</i>. An ability???? I don't do magic tricks with it. Unless you want to see how easily I can swallow large painkillers with barely a mouthful of water so I don't vomit!!!!! <br /><br /><br />Okay. I get where the idea of this character is coming from. And there are aspects to the descriptions surrounding Cyra's pain that I really liked.<br /><i>The pain was just part of life now. Simple tasks took twice as long because I had to pause for breath</i><br />Great stuff! The normality of everyday living changes completely when you live with chronic pain. You don't have an off switch from it, you have different levels of intensity and somehow you get through a day. And everything takes so very long. Even something as simple as getting out of bed in the morning can take hours. If anyone is interested in understanding more about the life of someone with a chronic illness I would love to direct you to "The Spoon Theory". It's a very simplistic but beautiful way of expressing what daily life can be like for chronic illness and pain sufferers. I would encourage anyone to read up on it so you can understand what normality is for those people like me who live under the radar with our invisible diseases. You can read all about it <a href="https://butyoudontlooksick.com/articles/written-by-christine/the-spoon-theory/" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>.<br /><br /><br />So here's another problem with the portrayal of chronic pain in the book. It may be stated once or twice that simple tasks take longer etc but I saw no extended periods of fatigue as a result. Cyra was frequently able to fight in a gym type environment... Really??? Like ALL of the time????? Trust me. There are days that no matter how much you try to push through the pain you can't. You just can't. There is insufferable and unending fatigue. <br /><br /><br />Also, if Cyra was truly in as much pain as she was, she would absolutely have been an insomniac as was stated in the book (case in point I'm writing this review at 4am) but she also would have, at times, passed out from the pain. However, there was one lovely quote I liked that I could very much identify with: <i>That he couldn't feel pain also meant he didn't know about the grey space just beneath consciousness that made it more bearable.</i> I love that grey space. I frequently stay hours in that grey space and don't know where my day has disappeared to all of a sudden. So I needed more moments like this. More explanations to ground Cyra's pain in reality. Pain so often should have consumed her body so much that she would have laid there motionless until unconscious. You often cannot take the pain and that needs to be shown more. It goes to this whole romanticised notion of pain. How suffering is some great beauty. <br /><br /><br />That brings me to chapter 25 (mild spoiler ahead) <br />In this chapter Cyra comes to the conclusion that ultimately <i>the gift is the strength the curse has given me... I can bear it. I can bear pain. I can bear anything.</i><br />This is insulting and wrong on so many levels. I know that ideologically this is a lovely thought. It goes to the idea that being someone living with pain and fighting through to live another day is admirable. <br />Look at how stoic she is, so brave, so strong.... <br />So spare me your melodrama!!! <br />That is an idea for people who don't live with daily pain. It is there, to comfort them. To justify why some people live lives of pain and others don't. It goes to the notion that pain is a burden which is only given to those who are strong enough to carry it. <br />Not true. <br />Pain is indiscriminate. Pain corrupts. Pain infiltrates your every fibre of person. It changes you. You don't become strong you become institutionalised to it. You fall back on survival mechanisms. Don't glorify those mechanisms as some sort of admirable strength. I don't want to bear "anything" thanks. The pain is quite enough. <br />It also alludes to a dangerous concept that as pain sufferers we somehow have this skill or ability to take more and more and more. As if we should never feel that the pain is too much??? <br />Trust me, with chronic pain the pain is MUCH too much, and this concept that Cyra thinks that her ability to bear incalculable amounts of pain makes her somehow strong is insulting. <br />It is okay to not be able to bear unending pain every day. <br />It is okay to feel like it is too much. <br />It is okay to need help. <br />It is okay to not have to suffer in silence. <br />It is okay to not have to be martyred by pain. <br /><br /><br />I would also like to have seen a greater emotional impact on Cyra of what it is like to live with pain for so long. I too was a child when pain took hold. I will never forget that first day of experiencing pain. What it was like ripping through my little body. <br />So where was the hatred? The bitterness?? The why me??? <br />The only self loathing we had on Cyra's part was because of how she inflicted her pain on others and her guilt over that. (Btw, also offensive. I would never wish my pain on another soul so to say that that is something a chronic pain sufferer would do... Yeah... Not impressed!) But I would have much preferred this loathing to be based on the manifestation of her pain and not some outside event. <br /><br /><br />I haven't even touched on the idea that Cyra's love interest in this story lessens her pain which just adds this book to the myriad of other YA novels out there that tells the reader that love can cure no matter what ails you be it a mental health issue or a physical illness.... At the end of the day, this is a fictional story and Cyra does not suffer from a chronic illness per se (I'm incredibly aware that in future books there is a possibility for a narrative surrounding healing which I hope the author will not explore). But as this is fictional who am I to say that the experiences of Cyra shouldn't be written as they are. Veronica Roth has claimed that she experiences chronic pain and perhaps this is how she feels... It just is not my experience of life with pain and not the experience of many other people who live with chronic pain that I am familiar with. <br /><br /><br />On the whole this is a very problematic book. <br />It has issues with poor writing and character development to start with. There are potentially offensive racial undertones, an unflagged trigger warning regarding self-harm and what I believe is an ineffectual representation of chronic pain. <br /><br /><br />But I don't think that Veronica Roth set out to be racist or ableist or any such thing. I believe that she is just a writer very much out of her depth lacking in proper guidance. I feel there is a sad indictment on the publishing industry that somehow allowed this book to slip through editing and proof reading with the presence of so many questionable aspects. <br /><br />So my last thoughts on this book are for Ms Roth and for her future writings. <br /><blockquote>In the words of the great Samuel Beckett:<br /><i>"Ever tried, ever failed, no matter. <br />Try again, fail again, fail better." </i></blockquote><br /><br /><br /><b>one star</b><br /><br /><br />---------<br /><br />Reading this with my favourite book group.<br /><br /><br /><b>Some pre-reading/viewing surrounding the controversies:</b><br /><br /><a href="http://justinaireland.com/dammit-this-is-a-blog/2016/12/4/the-continent-carve-the-mark-and-the-trope-of-the-dark-skinned-aggressor" rel="nofollow noopener">Justina Ireland Blog: The Trope of the Dark Skinned Agressor</a><br /><br /><a href="http://sabaatahir.tumblr.com/post/156055223595/how-can-you-support-veronica-roths-book-its" rel="nofollow noopener">Saaba Tahir's defence of the racism issues </a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.npr.org/templates/transcript/transcript.php?storyId=509650409&amp;ft=nprml&amp;f=509650409" rel="nofollow noopener">Veronica Roth's 'Carve The Mark' Is A Fantasy Inspired By Chronic Pain : NPR</a><br /><br /><a href="http://jennytrout.com/?p=11089" rel="nofollow noopener">This gift sucks Veronica, where do I return it. Blog post: Trout Nation</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.usatoday.com/story/life/books/2017/01/05/veronica-roth-carve-the-mark-divergent-facebook-live-chat/96011678/" rel="nofollow noopener">Video Chat Carve the Mark (in particular watch between 10 and 12.5 minutes)</a><br /><br />It has also been brought to my attention how the "kill marks" that are placed on certain characters skin in this book could be triggering to anyone with issues surrounding self-harm. So if that is something that affects you please be advised. <br />Here are two of my Goodreads friends reviews that are able to better express the issues surrounding that: <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1782763262" rel="nofollow noopener">Amber's review</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1782320836" rel="nofollow noopener">Caitlin's review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15279458785036085318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1792322909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792322909" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1792322909?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/33800852-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=gr_awards_2017">gr_awards_2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1792322909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6157029181088101036">Three things:<br/><br/>1. This book tries to YA too hard<br/>2. This book tries to Sci-fi too hard<br/>3. This book tries to world build too hard<br/><br/>I do give it 3 stars because overall I found it enjoyable, but the the things above distracted me so much. (Note: Lowered to two stars on 10/17/2017 because I thought I already gave it two and I keep thinking back to how much I didn't care for it . . . so, I had to drop it!)<br/><br/>YA - There is a general YA formula, but if you mix it in well with a creative story, it doesn't matt</span>
  <span id="freeText6157029181088101036" style="display:none">Three things:<br /><br />1. This book tries to YA too hard<br />2. This book tries to Sci-fi too hard<br />3. This book tries to world build too hard<br /><br />I do give it 3 stars because overall I found it enjoyable, but the the things above distracted me so much. (Note: Lowered to two stars on 10/17/2017 because I thought I already gave it two and I keep thinking back to how much I didn't care for it . . . so, I had to drop it!)<br /><br />YA - There is a general YA formula, but if you mix it in well with a creative story, it doesn't matter if it has the same themes and general plot lines. This book wore YA on its sleeve - young love between enemies, siblings trying to save each other, every main character except the protagonists parents is between the age of 14 and 19. I could go on.<br /><br />Sci-fi - I am still not sure why interplanetary travel was important in this story, but it happened. Mysterious powers that just so happen to be the most advantageous to the person who has them or convenient to the storyline. It really felt like Roth just wanted this book to be in space and threw out some special high tech weirdness to make it feel like other Sci-fi YA offerings (I was frequently reminded of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839976.Red_Rising__Red_Rising_Saga___1_" title="Red Rising (Red Rising Saga, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a> - which I did not care for very much)<br /><br />World building - Oh man, names, locations, traditions, races - one big confusing mashup! This distracted me the most. So many weird names and odd relationships I had a hard time keeping track of what was going on. The locations and travel were not very clear (see Sci-fi above). I couldn't tell if they were on one planet, several planets, what the ultimate political structure was, etc. Maybe all this is clear for some, but I was lost a lot of the time. <br /><br />Despite all of this, though, I did enjoy the story and was not disappointed in the plot and cliffhangers for a sequel. I just hope Roth doesn't try so hard to do what is expected.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6157029181088101036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1888480804" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1888480804?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khurram" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khurram" href="/user/show/25493797-khurram">Khurram</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1888480804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17078097368153778224">I was very disappointed with this book. Maybe after Divergent my expectations were too high, and it probably not fair to compare the tow although when a book is released saying the writer of Divergent it is hard not to expect a lot and compare the two. Also knowing Veronica Roth was a Star Wars fan and I am a Star Wars fan I figured what could possible go wrong.<br/><br/>The book is very slow then as soon as something exciting happens it is the end of the chapter and the moment is lost. Worse still in som</span>
  <span id="freeText17078097368153778224" style="display:none">I was very disappointed with this book. Maybe after Divergent my expectations were too high, and it probably not fair to compare the tow although when a book is released saying the writer of Divergent it is hard not to expect a lot and compare the two. Also knowing Veronica Roth was a Star Wars fan and I am a Star Wars fan I figured what could possible go wrong.<br /><br />The book is very slow then as soon as something exciting happens it is the end of the chapter and the moment is lost. Worse still in some cases of the cross over of the chapters it could be a couple of minutes later, a couple of hours, a day or in one case 2 years. There are a few short but brutal fight scattered around the book. Unfortunately for me there was not particularly well written. I know she thanks a friend who helped her choreograph the fight now in my mind I don't see how someone can strike with a knife with one hand then simultaneously (still in a standing position), remove a hidden blade from their boot and stab the person with it? The narration of the book is split between the two main characters. Cyra Noavek and Akos Kereseth. Like in the Divergent I think Veronica Roth is better a writing the female characters like Cyra. There are also mistakes in Akos narration (yes my grammar is not great so if I noticed it obvious), it is supposed to be first person like Cyra's but as he moves around it keeps he moved here or there he did that like someone is watching him.<br /><br />Here the Current is the energy/life force believed to flow through everyone. It bestows gifts on everyone some good, some bad and some useless. these gifts seem to be extensions of the person personalities. it is unknown if the person personality brings their "gift" or if they are this way because they are going to receive a certain "gift". The Current also seems to be harnessed in machines and is the basis for most of their technology. There are also the Oracles people who have been gifted to see the future, but they seem to be a law on to themselves. <br /><br />The planet Thuvhe is home to both the Thuvhe and Shotet people. Even though it is know interplanetary as Thuvhe. This because the Thuvhe farmers control the worlds biggest export of Hush and Ice flowers. The Shotet seem to be the more vicious and warrior people, and are known for marking kills by scaring their arms. Even though they are supposed to be the more "closed off" society they are more traveled people as part of their religious believes is a annual sojourn to a planet directed by the Currents and take there discarded technology and "garbage" back for renewal. When the Oracles decide to make peoples fates public the Shotet people make a daring move against the Thuvhe and Akos' family in general. Ryzek Noavek the ruler of Shotet (and Cyra's brother) will do anything to change his fate and show his people he is not weak.<br /><br />As much as I wanted to like this book I just don't, it is slow paced then skips ahead and tries to fill in blanks later. Also for suck a big book. Not much seems to happen for me too much stuff is left undone especially by the end of the book. if like me you have been fans Roth's previous books, all I can say it did not live up to my expectations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17078097368153778224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883826037?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)" href="/user/show/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky">Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883826037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6028673917825340423">This book already has 70k reviews and ratings... fml. <br/><br/>This book is interesting not because of it's story (which is dull) but <b>because of the circumstances surrounding it's release.</b> <br/><br/><b>BLACK FACE</b><br/><br/>Every now and then a book comes along that presents some toxic ideas which are commonly seen in tons of books. But our GoodReads community turns into a hive mind and decides this <i>one book</i> is the absolute worst. <br/><br/>I can't help but feel that this book got unlucky. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_' title='The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner's Curse</a> was gushed about despite it's </span>
  <span id="freeText6028673917825340423" style="display:none">This book already has 70k reviews and ratings... fml. <br /><br />This book is interesting not because of it's story (which is dull) but <b>because of the circumstances surrounding it's release.</b> <br /><br /><b>BLACK FACE</b><br /><br />Every now and then a book comes along that presents some toxic ideas which are commonly seen in tons of books. But our GoodReads community turns into a hive mind and decides this <i>one book</i> is the absolute worst. <br /><br />I can't help but feel that this book got unlucky. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> was gushed about despite it's disgusting representation of colonialism and slavery. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1628676504?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Maas</a> had published a dozen books, short stories and novellas before readers started to grumble about the lack of LGBT characters. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14395011.Mark_Lawrence__Prince_of_Thorns" title="Mark Lawrence, Prince of Thorns" rel="nofollow noopener">Mark Lawrence, Prince of Thorns</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108424.Patrick_Rothfuss" title="Patrick Rothfuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick Rothfuss</a> got almost no flack for their sexist stereotypes. <br /><br />So the question becomes- <b>are people outraged by the offensive stereotypes or are they just unable to ignore them because the story was subpar?</b> <br /><br />Race in fantasy is a difficult thing. Most writers avoid it entirely, <b>it's a chronic truism that if the book is a fantasy then you can assume everyone is white</b>. In <i>Carve the Mark</i> I'm not sure there was any way for Roth to avoid this controversy. She set up a situation in which two cultures clash. Providing any sort of racial markers to either group was going to cause a reaction. <br /><br />For the criticism of ableism- all I can really add is people who experience disability or chronic pain are likely to have the clearest perspective on this but since there are entire spiritual practices devoted to incorporating pain into knowledge of god it would probably be useful to remember that there is not <i>one</i> right way to write about difficult experiences. The most useful discussion around this stuff is seeing if the writer correctly identified a <i>possible</i> response to a human experience. They aren't representing <i>your</i> experience. If every time a writer tried to write about an experience they don't have personal knowledge of they got lambasted… well good luck getting <i>any</i> marginalised experiences into print. <br /><br />Perhaps the backlash against this novel will be an important marker to writers and publishers alike? God knows I've gritted my teeth thru enough "white saviour", "black aggressor", "magical negro" and "noble savage" stereotypes to be eager to see these tropes die out. Maybe Roth's new book is the bloody sacrifice needed to make publishers sit up and take notice? In which case this mediocre book can be said to have done some real good in the literary world. <br /><br />But I can't help suspecting this novel will be thrown on a pyre righteous of indignation like other outliers before it is ignobly forgotten. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Readers will continue to eat up sexist and racist stories because the characters are swoon worthy, the plot is thrilling or the reader's who object are "oversensitive sjw's".</b>
</i> <br /><br />This controversy is food for thought for writers and readers alike. Despite what some people claim <b>stories are important cultural indicators</b>. They shape and define how we experience and respond to the world around us. A story is never "just a story" and I'm pleased to see so many fellow readers engaging with subtext and connotation, rather then reviews full of gifs saying "omfg love interest is soooo hawt". <br /><br /><br /><b>BLOOD MONEY</b> <br /><br /><br />The second thing worth noting was the <b>volume of paid reviews</b> this book has on the front page. There are a ton of studies that show how <i>being financially paid to review a product unconsciously inflates reviewers' scores</i>. This is the first novel I've come across on GR were the front page was saturated with paid reviews. GR has been fiercely defended as a place created for readers by readers (and the bloody remnants of many writing careers can still be found scattered across the site). <br /> <br />In a world of tightly controlled image creation GR members have managed to carve out a space that can be downright vicious to anyone who tries to infiltrate the community for commercial purposes. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>As a community we need to think carefully about accepting paid reviews as a common practice.</b>
</i> It destroys authenticity. Most regular users are voracious readers. It would be wonderful if we could all earn a living by reading books. But here's the thing: <b>you won't</b>. Even if a tiny fraction of readers manage to earn a living wage reviewing books it will be at the cost of their personal integrity and the community's effectiveness. Goodreads works because it is real. It is genuine word of mouth supercharged across the globe. Marketers might be drooling to get a slice of the PR pie but we as members decide whether that is organic, authentic acclaim or... not.<br /><br />There is a very real risk if this trend continues that GR will become an advertisement billboard. Our choices now will determine the future of goodreads. <br /><br /><b>If you see a review that is paid for don't like it. Let the other member know you are unhappy with their decision to accept payment for a review.</b> These are two really easy things members can do to curb these trends. If paid reviews get no "likes" and languish on the 20th page publishers won't bother trying to curate the book's image. Likewise, if members see that accepting paid reviews breaks their friends trust, they won't accept them. <br /><br />How we address commercial encroachment in Good Reads matters. <b>I don't come to GR to read 30 paid ads on the book I'm about to read, do you?</b><br /><br />Edit: Some booktubers and reviewers have vigorously defended themselves. I wanted to add evidence to my claim that the inflation in reviews occurs <i>
  <b>even where the reviewers believe they are being objective</b>
</i>:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://reviewmeta.com/blog/analysis-of-7-million-amazon-reviews-customers-who-receive-free-or-discounted-item-much-more-likely-to-write-positive-review/">https://reviewmeta.com/blog/analysis-...</a><br /><br />Although this refers to amazon reviews I think it provides sufficient evidence for the same problem on GR.<br /><br />For further evidence of how fucked up it is having sponsored reviews on goodreads see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789138449?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Riley's review </a> Which describes how her contact was <b>dissolved</b> when she notified the publisher she would be writing a negative review. <br /><br />Edit: Fixed formatting/ spelling/ added links.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6028673917825340423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14517386914017453145">this book reminds me of preteen me, meaning it tries too hard to fit in with all the cool kids. oof. not a good look for anyone involved. <i>trust me.</i><br/><br/>this book tries a little too hard to be YA relatable, to be sci-fi intense, and to have the most fantastic world ever built. and i think because there is so much focus on all of these different elements, it neglects one major component - THE PLOT. my goodness. its practically nonexistent. combine that with some slow pacing and you get many bored reade</span>
  <span id="freeText14517386914017453145" style="display:none">this book reminds me of preteen me, meaning it tries too hard to fit in with all the cool kids. oof. not a good look for anyone involved. <i>trust me.</i><br /><br />this book tries a little too hard to be YA relatable, to be sci-fi intense, and to have the most fantastic world ever built. and i think because there is so much focus on all of these different elements, it neglects one major component - THE PLOT. my goodness. its practically nonexistent. combine that with some slow pacing and you get many bored readers. i wasnt so bored that i couldnt be bothered to finish it, because there were some parts that actually interested me, but i did feel my eyes glaze over from time to time.<br /><br />but the concept still remained interesting to me throughout, even if i had to trudge through it. and i thought the characters were relatable and engaging enough. i do think they took a backseat to all of the world building, which is a shame. but i was invested enough to care about seeing how everything worked out in the end. <br /><br />overall, this has its ups and downs. its a pretty average read, and not one i would particularly recommend to anyone, but i dont regret reading it.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3 stars</i></b></span>
