    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1639798912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1639798912" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1639798912?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008159481" href="/book/show/30233110-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=arc-physical-pusblisher">arc-physical-pusblisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need">physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1639798912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3699202593634400106"><i>I'd like to put a disclaimer for all the controversy surrounding this novel. I read this before anyone and didn't see the underlying issues everyone saw with the story until a few of my friends told me about all the explosions on social media sites I don't even have. I did still adore this story, I'd be lying if I said I didn't, but I don't want to offend anyone by liking this book. I want everyone to know I can't possibly relate to these issues, but my eyes are open and I understand people are </i></span>
  <span id="freeText3699202593634400106" style="display:none"><i>I'd like to put a disclaimer for all the controversy surrounding this novel. I read this before anyone and didn't see the underlying issues everyone saw with the story until a few of my friends told me about all the explosions on social media sites I don't even have. I did still adore this story, I'd be lying if I said I didn't, but I don't want to offend anyone by liking this book. I want everyone to know I can't possibly relate to these issues, but my eyes are open and I understand people are hurt. Please understand it is not my intention to support something wrong or to hurt anyone...I am just keeping my review as is because it's how I felt about the story-candidly.</i><br><br><p>
  <a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/Carve%20the%20Mark%20Quote_zpswovbk5j4.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478016522i/21021275._SX540_.png" alt=" photo Carve the Mark Quote_zpswovbk5j4.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><p><br><br>Wow. I just…there are times when the words flow out of me in torrents and I can’t stop no matter how hard I try, but then there are times when I have literally one million things to say…and <b>no idea how to say them</b>. This book touched me in a way I’m not often used to-at least, not anymore. A long time ago, when I finally found my favorite genres and what made me the happiest, I was finding a seamless stream of five star books because I had finally found what <i>worked</i> for me. But lately, those streams of winners are harder to come by.<br><br>For one, <b>I’m extremely picky now</b>-I know what I like, down to the very last word, and anything less is unacceptable. It’s no secret to any of my friends that I love all things mayhem, death, destruction, forbidden love mixed with peril peril peril. But <b>not many authors truly, <i>truly</i> give you all those things at once</b>. It’s so rare, anyway. And, because it’s so rare, those authors who <i>do</i> deliver on all things nasty and despicable in the name of love make it impossible to forget who they are.</p><br><p>
  
    <strong>“You’re a Noavek,” he said stubbornly, folding his arms. “Brutality is in your blood.”</strong>
  
</p><br><p>I have this little niche of what I like to call ‘peril authors’. They are my go-to when I want something that isn’t always rainbows and unicorns. Now, I’m not saying the stories don’t eventually end happily…but <b>they leave you with some very nasty cliffhangers</b>. Did I happen to mention that nasty, white-knuckle cliffhangers are literally <u>my favorite thing EVER</u>?? So, these authors, <b>they never shy away from doing what they need to pack a devastating punch</b>. I never go all in when my head isn’t in the right place-after all, even the most dastardly and peril obsessed reviewers need a break from all the heart-break. We aren’t robots, ya know?? And, after a while, if you read hardcore books one after the other, you are bound to become a little bit jaded.</p><br><p>
  <a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/giphy%205_zpseagjcqv0.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <span>[image error]</span>
  </a>
</p><br><p>So, when I was offered this beauty from the publishers of Veronica Roth’s newest MASTERPIECE, I, of course, accepted. For one, what an honor-little ol’ me, getting a book from a best-selling MEGA FAMOUS author before most of the world. It’s crazy, and I did not look a gift horse in mouth-I didn’t hesitate in responding. Secondly, I adored-ABSOLUTELY ADORED-the Divergent trilogy. And not just the first two-all three. <b>Veronica Roth</b>, while <b>a very cunning and devious woman</b>, is someone I wholly admire. Her writing is poetic and flows effortlessly from paragraph to paragraph, page to page. <b>I have ALWAYS lumped her in with my favorite poetic authors</b>.</p><br><p><strong>“A knife,” I said. “A hot poker. A rusty nail.”</strong><br><br> <strong> “You are more than any of those things.”</strong></p><br><p>And, while she isn’t someone I think of weekly, or even monthly, I have never forgotten her after her shocking finale to the Divergent series. The ‘what-if’s and ‘what will she do next’s were never far from my mind…it has just taken a while to finally see a new book in the works from this spectacular woman.</p><br><p>
  
    <strong>“And you’re starting to sound kind of cocky, for someone I routinely beat up.”</strong>
  
</p><br><p>I know many people are weary of what comes next from the daring author who shocked the world (and that is the LAST time I will mention her former series, because it is doing a great injustice to this beautiful book), and I know there are going to be a <i>million</i> comparisons-it’s just inevitable. But I truly saw something so amazing here-something I never thought I’d see. <b>It would be such a shame to not give this duology a chance because of an uncertain future and phobia of the past</b>. I know everyone is quick to fall in love with main characters (I fell so hard, so fast for these two new characters that it shocked even me) and people are quick to protect those they love---but <b>the love I feel for these two AMAZING characters is so unparalleled</b>, and <b>permanent</b>, that I must <u>insist</u> on reading this the moment it comes out.</p><br><p>
  <a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_nlix172VDH1tqou9go1_500_zpswrbdttgx.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478016522ra/21021278.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_nlix172VDH1tqou9go1_500_zpswrbdttgx.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><p><strong>When I looked at him again, he was smiling at me hesitantly.</strong><br><br> <strong>“You love them,” he said. “All these places, all these things.”</strong></p><br><p>I’ll admit that I was scared of the prospect of space travel-and for that matter, space lingo-but <b>not once did I ever slow down or feel lost</b> as I was racing through this fast-paced, addicting story. And that’s my favorite thing-<b>I never wanted to put this book down</b>. Roth’s passion was reflected on each and every page, echoing to us in a new, inventive way with each arising issue. Each character was created in a delicate manner, making for layered, flawed, and believable characters. <b>These were people you wanted to root for</b>, and you never really knew if they were going to win-in both mental and physical scenarios.</p><br><p>
  
    <strong>"You and I, we’ve become what we were made to become.”</strong>
  
</p><br><p>Their minds were tested in unimaginable and barbaric ways, twisting what they believed and hoped for in life to the point of utter despair. Loyalties were bent and broken, repaired and restored-the boundaries of love and family snuffed out in a manner of minutes. <b>You were forced to pick a side and survive</b>…whether you wanted to or not.</p><br><p>
  <strong>
    The same thing she always did, only now he noticed-noticed that he knew it, that was; knew her routines, knew <i>her</i>.<br><br> 
  </strong>
  <strong>
    And liked her.
  </strong>
</p><br><p>Akos is from the peace loving Thuvhe, a wintery world where you have to wear goggles to walk around outside. It’s beauty is unparalleled to its inhabitants, crystallized and serene and snowy as can be. Grays are the norm, much like the environment…which can be seen as dull to others. Cyra is Noavek-Brutal and unforgiving Shotet tyrants who wear blue. Their beliefs couldn’t be any different, nor could the difference in style of life: One place bloodthirsty, unrelenting in its quest for power and dominance. <b>Pain is no stranger here</b>. You can immediately see why our two main characters are the way they are, and you instantly feel for both. Sides are hard to choose and <b>lines are blurred</b>…as becomes evident the farther into the story we get.</p><br><p>
  <a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_inline_nxn35woTO51rhf55x_500_zpsn2esyffa.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478016522ra/21021279.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_nxn35woTO51rhf55x_500_zpsn2esyffa.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><p>And here comes the good stuff, the stuff that makes this beautiful love story possible. <b>Forbidden love</b>…isn’t it the best thing ever, when done correctly? Yeah. I think so, too. Cyra’s currentgift is pain, Akos’s is to diffuse people’s gift. Both very valuable currentgifts…and <b>both susceptible to manipulation and vulnerable to almost everyone</b>. When paired together without a say in the matter, they realize they can be an asset to one another. <b>Neither is willing to put all their trust in the other</b>, but they also don’t fight what seems to be a tentative alliance. After all, it’s nice having someone who understands you (to a degree), someone who is there to take some of the burden away, who wants to help (again, to a degree-they <i>do</i> have differing conclusions to what they believe to be their story).</p><br><p>
  <strong>
    “Honor,” I said with a snort. “Honor has no place in survival.”
  </strong>
</p><br><p>But, as they get closer, what was once clear begins to become a convoluted cloud of emotions and hope-<b>could they possibly want the same thing</b>?? Is she truly a monster, or can she still be someone who helps make the world a better place? Does she <i>want</i> to help Akos…even at the expense of going against her only brother?</p><br><p>
  <a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/8735574_zps30bjjtsy.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478016522ra/21021280.gif" alt=" photo 8735574_zps30bjjtsy.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><p>Akos’s kindness was something that resonated deeply within me right away-but, even more than that, his gradual <b>fierceness</b>. He’s not perfect, nor is he indestructible, but his silent fury mixed with an unrelenting kindness made him an instant book boyfriend that <b>I was absolutely obsessed</b> with. And then Cyra-<b>one of my favorite female leads of all time</b>. Some might say I even have a girl crush. Yeah-serious stuff, right?</p><br><p>
  <strong>
     “Next time, when something that sounds remarkably like war drums is going to wake me at dawn, could you maybe warn me?”
  </strong>
</p><br><p>Cyra deals with pain 24/7. Literally-all day, all night-no matter what. Until she dispenses that pain into an unwilling victim, causing them pain so severe they would reveal their deepest, darkest secrets. She is numb to the power now, her brother’s little torture device. Cunning, witty, and skilled in combat like nobody’s business, she is not to be trifled with-seriously, she’s so bad<i>ass</i>. But-and probably why my girl crush (on top of my book boyfriend crush (so much win)) is shining so bright-<b>she wasn’t so strong she didn’t have vulnerability or weakness</b>. She lost sometimes. She didn’t always make the right choices. And, if I’m comparing here, I kept thinking of a female book character I really didn’t like...she kind of made up the anatomy of Cyra, here.</p><br><p>
  <strong>
    It was not hope; it did not soar; it slithered, clawed, and dragged, and it would not let me stop.
  </strong>
</p><br><p>
  <a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_nqne0kQwpF1sy9gl7o1_500_zpsj939po1k.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478016522i/21021281._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_nqne0kQwpF1sy9gl7o1_500_zpsj939po1k.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><p>I saw a lot Adelina from Marie Lu’s most recent trilogy. Dark, corrupted, and <b>willing to do what she had to for those she loved</b>-and herself. She had to relieve the pain sometimes, you know? It’s not all about choice. But, see, I hated Adelina. She was okay, I guess, but I found her pathetic and whiny-not here. Cyra took the BEST PARTS of Adelina and made her someone I <u>adored</u>. Okay, I didn’t really read the second or third books of that trilogy, nor is there a direct line that connected these characters in any way-I just got the vibe, that feeling, and I dug it.</p><br><p>
  
    <strong>"I like to move."<br><br> </strong>
  
  <strong>"I've noticed."</strong>
</p><br><b>She is a tool of destruction</b>, of torture, she is a key to be used in war<b>-she can bring any one person to their knees</b> with her amazing power-but she is vulnerable to the pain, and to herself-<b>she is resigned to be the monster she was fated to be</b>. But not ONCE does she whine about it-it’s her life and she lives with it daily…And I found that so amazing. She just goes about her life in suffering, trying to (at Akos’s influence) be the best she can be. And, again, she doesn’t always succeed. Did I mention I love her? And Akos? And I ship them? Hm. Well. I’ll say it again: <b>they are everything to me</b>.<br><p>
  
    <strong>He offered touch to me so freely, without realizing how rare it was. How rare <i>he</i> was, to a person like me.</strong>
  
</p><br><p>
  <a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/11371326_zpsastvjo3n.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478016522ra/21021282.gif" alt=" photo 11371326_zpsastvjo3n.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><p>So, as you can see, I’m hooked. I was hooked from the first part that was in his POV, and I was sunk-line and sinker-when I met Cyra. <b>These two were made for one another</b>, but born enemies. They don’t want to like each other, and they don’t always understand, but...things happen. And isn’t slow burn romance the <b>best</b> kind of romance (especially paired with forbidden romance-HA thought you caught me there, didn’t you)?? Roth’s writing was, as promised, better than ever and even <b>a bit more mature</b>, if that’s even possible. She writes in a way you don’t once get confused about, no matter the content, and makes you physically ache for more. It’s been a long time since I was so stressed out I couldn’t breathe, but <b>more than once I found myself gasping for breath and clutching my heart</b>-stopping and staring at the page with wide eyes as I tried to calm my breathing (maybe this partially has to do with being pregnant, but I say no, I was just super excitable because...excellence at work, people) and get myself under control. I smiled so big without even realizing it that it bordered on embarrassing. I tried, and failed, repeatedly to find errors with the book and why my best of friends wouldn’t like the story (or anyone, for that matter, if I’m being honest), but never once could think of anything. And, if there <i>was</i> something, it was nit-picky and I completely missed it. I don’t know if this book is for everybody, or even what everyone else will think-All I can do is go with my heart and my gut, and they both say <b>this is a winner</b>. I know, without a doubt, that when this releases it will be my (late) Christmas gift to all friends and family that read. I know it’s a certainty I will be rushing to Barnes and Noble on release day to buy myself a hardback of this new absolute favorite. I have found three favorite books this year, all by amazing authors almost everyone loves…and <b>this book tops them all</b>. So, my hope is, with this long-winded review, that I’ve convinced or intrigued almost everyone to give this book a shot. And, for those who are not so easily swayed (or manipulated), honestly, its their loss.</p><br><p> </p><br><br><p>
  <strong>
    <em>**Quotes taken from an uncorrected galley and are subject to change upon release of the finished book**</em>
  </strong>
</p><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1712666858" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1712666858" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712666858?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=the-final-frontier">the-final-frontier</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712666858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3078753983938001040"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/> <br/><b>Divergent Wars: One Force will define you. </b><br/><br/><br/><br/>Curious (and polite) people kept asking me if I was enjoying CARVE THE MARK while I was reading it. For the flippant response to that question, please refer to the opening of the song <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6mEMfxFEaXw' rel='nofollow noopener'>"Nobody But Me"</a> by The Human Beinz. Or, you know, check out my star rating. (But my way is more fun, and you get a fun song out of it, too!)<br/><br/><br/><br/>I was one of the few people who did not like DIVERGENT. Part of that was </span>
  <span id="freeText3078753983938001040" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br> <br><b>Divergent Wars: One Force will define you. </b><br><br><br><br>Curious (and polite) people kept asking me if I was enjoying CARVE THE MARK while I was reading it. For the flippant response to that question, please refer to the opening of the song <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6mEMfxFEaXw" rel="nofollow noopener">"Nobody But Me"</a> by The Human Beinz. Or, you know, check out my star rating. (But my way is more fun, and you get a fun song out of it, too!)<br><br><br><br>I was one of the few people who did not like DIVERGENT. Part of that was the world-building that didn't make sense, and part of that was what I perceived as jarring anti-intellectualism. You might say I'm being oversensitive. Maybe. Or maybe the author's choice to make the intellectual faction into what were basically a bunch of fascists did not sit well with me. And no, I'm not just saying that because I scored as "erudite" in that stupid faction quiz. (Well, mostly. *sniff, sniff* I'm <i>not </i>a fascist!)<br><br><br><br>When I heard that Roth was penning a <i>new </i>series of books, I was skeptical. Especially when it was being blurbed as a cross between Star Wars and DIVERGENT. I liked <i>one </i>of those things very much, but would space opera and the compelling promise of vengeance and battles be enough to compensate for the DIVERGENT similarities? And, more importantly, how would her style evolve? Or would it be more BS about smart people wrecking society and brave people jumping out of trains?<br><br><br><br>CARVE THE MARK is a very weird book - and, to its credit, is a very different story from DIVERGENT. It's about the Thuhve, a "peace-loving" people, and the Shotet, an opportunistic and war-like people who are ruled by a "tyrant" and who carve marks denoting their kills into their forearms. Akos, the Thuhvian, is taken capture by the Shotet's ruler, Rhyzek, along with his brother, because his brother has the power of prophecy. Cyra is Rhyzek's sister, and has the ability to cause people incredible pain - or even death - upon physical contact. Rhyzek uses her to do his dirty work and to put fear into his people.<br><br><br><br>The power source in this book is something called the "current," which from what I gathered is like a cross between the "Lifestream" in Final Fantasy VII and the Force in Star Wars. It's a physical thing of immense power that people can draw upon, creating "currentblades" (e.g. lightsabers) and being born with "currentgifts" (e.g. the Force) that manifest in different ways to do different things.<br><br><br><br>Okay, cool. A little derivative, but hey, super powers aren't exactly a novel concept, and I'm always down to read about them if done well. What's 100% original these days, anyway? Exactly.<br><br><br><br>But I could not get into CARVE THE MARK at all. It felt very amateurish. It was too long, and the characters were not developed at all. At least Tris had some emotional complexity to her and the romance between Four and Tris was compelling (and arguably the best part of the story). On the other hand, the romance between Cyra and Akos has zero chemistry, and when they start talking about being in love with each other it comes totally out of left field because, again, zero evidence for it (that I perceived - by that point, I was skimming pretty heavily, and I may have missed a telltale "clue").<br><br><br><br>CARVE THE MARK read like a very bad debut for me, with shoddy world building, a cliche and cowardly villain, and two heroes who don't really have any interesting personality traits or conflicts. I'm honestly shocked by how unpleasant the experience of reading this was, and if I had read this without knowing who the author was, I might have thought that this was a cleaned-up self-published effort or a debut tentatively put forth by a first-time (and very young) author.<br><br><br><br>I'm honestly disappointed because I love space opera - it's one of my favorite genres - and I was hoping to see a mainstream author write a glowing example of it, because if space opera boomed like the dystopian genre did in the late 2000s, I'd be one happy gal.<br><br><br><br>Maybe it will, but let's not make this book the poster child for the movement.<br><br><br><br>1 star.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3078753983938001040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Bibi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi"><img alt="Bibi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602128191p2/33411728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891224353?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibi" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi">Bibi</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891224353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14316901508382902552"><blockquote><b>01/26/2017</b><br/><br/>Having spent the last hour reading through <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1403417152' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review 1</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809204614?book_show_action=true&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review 2</a>, <a href='https://twitter.com/heatherezell/status/821145389885583361' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tweets</a>, <a href='http://aperfectioncalledbooks.blogspot.com.ng/2017/01/the-post-i-was-scared-to-write.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>opinion posts</a>, in addition to the comments threads, there seems to be a whole lot of furore about this book which, I must say, now has me intrigued enough to want to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30117284.Carve_the_Mark__Carve_the_Mark___1_' title='Carve the Mark (Carve the Mark, #1) by Veronica Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carve the Mark</a>. <br/><br/>A few reviewers felt the need to <b>disclaim previous reviews</b>, while some bloggers sought to distance themselves from both the author and HarperTeen, the publishers. My understanding is that one, the book has racial undertones, the aut</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14316901508382902552" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>01/26/2017</b><br /><br />Having spent the last hour reading through <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1403417152" rel="nofollow noopener">Review 1</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809204614?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Review 2</a>, <a href="https://twitter.com/heatherezell/status/821145389885583361" rel="nofollow noopener">Tweets</a>, <a href="http://aperfectioncalledbooks.blogspot.com.ng/2017/01/the-post-i-was-scared-to-write.html" rel="nofollow noopener">opinion posts</a>, in addition to the comments threads, there seems to be a whole lot of furore about this book which, I must say, now has me intrigued enough to want to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30117284.Carve_the_Mark__Carve_the_Mark___1_" title="Carve the Mark (Carve the Mark, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Carve the Mark</a>. <br /><br />A few reviewers felt the need to <b>disclaim previous reviews</b>, while some bloggers sought to distance themselves from both the author and HarperTeen, the publishers. My understanding is that one, the book has racial undertones, the author's allusion to chronic pain as a source of strength for one of the characters is another problematic issue.<br /><br /><b>Empathy, I understand.</b> What has me concerned is that I haven't read, yet, a review from a person of color. Should any of my friends have a review from a POC, please, feel free to share. Nevertheless, I will set aside the 20+ (laugh/scoff, you know you want to) "currently-reading" books to gladly dive into this one. <b>Will I find it offensive? Perhaps, but what I know you all know is, I'll be 100% real.</b></blockquote></span>

        <a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link1891224353" title="Flag this review as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=1891224353&amp;resource_type=Review&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F30117284-carve-the-mark">flag</a>





      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1891224353'><a id="like_count_review_1891224353" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1891224353?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">119 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F30117284-carve-the-mark">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_1884589250" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1884589250" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1884589250?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=a-z-ya-challenge-2017">a-z-ya-challenge-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=multi-povs">multi-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=great-premise-lacking-execution">great-premise-lacking-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=false-advertising">false-advertising</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884589250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1892907818373398493">Long review for a rather long read. I'm still struggling to figure what words are appropriate to describe the mediocrity and utter pointlessness of this book. My thoughts about it aren't as concise as this review will turn out being, because I only have so many words to fit in my review space and I want to illustrate why this book ended up being such a horrible experience. It's my worst read of 2017 thus far, though I considered giving it credit for at least the last quarter of the book holding </span>
  <span id="freeText1892907818373398493" style="display:none">Long review for a rather long read. I'm still struggling to figure what words are appropriate to describe the mediocrity and utter pointlessness of this book. My thoughts about it aren't as concise as this review will turn out being, because I only have so many words to fit in my review space and I want to illustrate why this book ended up being such a horrible experience. It's my worst read of 2017 thus far, though I considered giving it credit for at least the last quarter of the book holding my attention (Honestly though, slogging through 80% of this only to get to intriguing scenes of action/character stake investment? Not worth it, definitely not worth it) . I'm a fast reader, it wasn't the length of this book that deterred me - my library copy clocked in just around 460 some pages - but this book was such a tedious, offensive mess. <br /><br />Before I address the most pervasively discussed problems in this narrative (i.e. how racist and and ablelist this book is on several levels. There isn't an argument to be made about that - it exists in this book even if the author herself doesn't realize that it does in this narrative, and I picked up on it in several instances in this narrative, probably more than I can direct quote in this review. I'll do my best to illustrate these points using quotes from the text where I can, though), I'll discuss the aspects of this book that are a little easier for me to address in quick notation.<br /><br />As a bit of background, I had actually planned to read this book quite a while back. My experiences with Roth's books have been rocky to say the least. I thought "Divergent" was okay (though with issues), "Insurgent" was less okay (with more issues, but it held my attention still) and "Allegiant" was just...not good is putting it mildly. But I figured I'd give "Carve the Mark" a chance because it had all the bullet points of a series I might like. It's sci-fi, it's set in space, involves political intrigue and manipulation of powers/unique abilities of its cast, has some romantic inclinations, and involves a purportedly epic clash between different groups of people. (I'm deliberately ignoring the comparisons to Star Wars/X-Men because that sets up unrealistic expectations, and I don't buy into that kind of hype.) <br /><br />I started hearing about issues with this narrative on the day of release, and several of my Goodreads friends and trusted bloggers had mixed reactions to it as well. I'm thinking "Oh crud, glad I didn't preorder it. I still want to read it; maybe I should just get it from the library if it doesn't have ten billion holds." On one of my routine trips to my library, I saw the book on the shelf and was wondering like "Can I actually check this out?" Turns out I could, and I did, and my initial thoughts were whether I was lucky to get one or if I'd set myself up for disappointment.<br /><br />The long and short of "Carve the Mark's" story centers on the conflict between two space societies: the Thuvue and the Shotet. People in this world have unique abilities called currentgifts, which by definition in the glossary of the story "develop during puberty. They are not always benevolent." The story attempts to showcase the perspectives of Akos and Cyra from those nations respectively. Akos and his brother Eijeh, after a series of violent events, are kidnapped by the Shotet and made to use their currentgifts for the benefit of Cyra's family. Eijeh is subjected under the influence of Cyra's tyrannical brother Rhyzek, while Akos uses his abilities to aid Cyra. Cyra is a young woman whose existence is tormented by her currentgift, but yet she enacts her brother's will by serving as a weapon under his direct command. Cyra doesn't want to hurt anyone or serve as her brother's weapon in their kingdom, but her ability impedes her and can't escape the guilt of a secret (read: not so secret) that hangs over her head - both by her brother's influence and her own guilt. <br /><br />Cyra and Akos have a rocky relationship with competing interests at first, but as they learn about each other's experiences, they grow closer romantically and end up making plans to take Rhyzek down. Of course this journey isn't without a few curveballs (supposedly, I honestly didn't find them that shocking) the narrative throws at the reader in the end, and apparently leaves to continue in this purported duology.<br /><br />While this summary of the story wouldn't seem so terrible when taken by that barebones approach, there were so many things wrong with "Carve The Mark" in execution that it's difficult to know where to begin. The pacing in the novel is atrociously sluggish, starting with very little conflict or explanation and meandering more often than not (I found this to be a similar problem in Roth's "Alliegiant"). The worldbuilding is weakly drawn from the beginning, and the presentation of the world is awkward and confusing. For a book that blends sci-fi and fantasy in a space centered universe - there's never a chance to become immersed or invested in the environment. Granted, this is a universe where Oracles determine the fates of people with currentgifts and note how their gifts influence the balance of power between the societies. Akos and Cyra come from two powerful families and have powerful gifts that they develop over time, though there isn't much attention to the system by which this works (what little there is comes across as confusing). "Carve the Mark" trades between their perspectives, starting with Akos in third person, while Cyra's perspective is written in first person POV.<br /><br />It was hard to care for any of the cast of characters in this book other than Cyra. Cyra had the more prominent storyline and scenetime, while Akos's perspective suffered from being too emotionally distant despite some purportedly harrowing experiences. Add to the fact that Roth chose to telegraph certain experiences and emotions of the characters - withholding certain revelations key to the storyline for no particular reason at all (and you could guess what those revelations were without getting too far into the storyline - I predicted them fairly quickly.) The narrative would've benefited from them being shown and fleshed out much more than the attention they received. So, the writing and establishment of the plot was much weaker than it would've otherwise been with greater care and time taken to develop the world. Don't even get me started on the one-note side characters and villains. For a reportedly violent sci-fi world with prominent clashes, when certain characters bit the bullet, I found it hard to care because I really didn't feel like I knew the characters in this novel that well. Even Ryzek's motivations felt paperthin despite the attempt to showcase his flaws and eventually the rationale he uses to manipulate his sister into being his weapon of choice to enact his assertion of power. <br /><br />Cyra and Akos's characters had a few scenes where I could believe in their chemistry and slow burning relationship, but I felt my connection to them was shortchanged because of the way the narrative chose to not only push them together for convenient circumstance, but ultimately the narrative becoming another example in problematic YA tropes for <i>I can heal your problems with the power of love!</i> <br /><br />These are just the mentions of structural and narrative issues with "Carve the Mark" without mentioning the problematic presentation of themes and depictions in the work. And it's perhaps the racist and ableist depictions that showcase not only how lazy the construction of this work really was, but how it attempted to incorporate such themes in a flawed and insensitive way.<br /><br />It may be ironic of me to point out <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=uvGhuLTWezM" rel="nofollow noopener">this video of Roth talking about the importance of portrayal of race in this narrative</a> but I honestly think that despite the intention of *trying* to be inclusive of different races with her intentional incorporation of skin tones and hair textures - she completely misses the point of what it means to be inclusive. <br /><br />When you are writing minority characters accurately, you are dealing with more than just an incorporation of skin tones. I think that point bears repeating: <b> When you are writing minority characters accurately, you are dealing with more than just an incorporation of skin tones.</b> Part of the problem with certain portrayals of minority groups in fiction, including in sci-fi and fantasy, is that there's a history of harmful stereotypes of minority groups in comparison to White/Caucasian or majority groups. This stereotyping is very evident in numerous areas of "Carve the Mark". I felt that <a href="http://justinaireland.com/dammit-this-is-a-blog/2016/12/4/the-continent-carve-the-mark-and-the-trope-of-the-dark-skinned-aggressor" rel="nofollow noopener">Justina Ireland did a fine job of pointing out just a few of these problems</a> alongside <a href="http://justinaireland.com/dammit-this-is-a-blog/2016/12/6/please-show-your-work" rel="nofollow noopener">quoting some examples</a> where this is noted in the text. But these are only just a few examples.<br /><br />This book was ethnocentric from the very beginning against the Shotet group, and that never changed through the entire story.<br /><br />Chapter 1: <i>"The Shotet were a people, not a nation-planet, and they were known to be fierce, brutal. They stained lines into their arms for every life they had taken, and trained even their children in the art of war. And they lived on Thuvhe, the same planet as Akos and his family—though the Shotet didn’t call this planet “Thuvhe,” or themselves “Thuvhesits”—across a huge stretch of feathergrass. The same feathergrass that scratched at the windows of Akos’s family’s house." </i><br /><br /><i>“Sometimes it is easy to see why people become what they are,” his mom said softly. “Ryzek and Cyra, children of a tyrant. Their father, Lazmet, child of a woman who murdered her own brothers and sisters. The violence infects each generation.”</i> &lt;- This is Akos's mother telling him about how harmful the Shotet people are. (Prejudice is a dish served cold in this narrative, apparently.)<br /><br />Chapter 2: <i>Akos knew it without really knowing it: These men were Shotet. Enemies of Thuvhe, enemies of </i>theirs.<i> People like this were responsible for every candle lit in the memorial of the Shotet invasion; they had scarred Hessa’s buildings, busted its glass so it showed fractured images; they had culled the bravest, the strongest, the fiercest, and left their families to weeping. Akos’s grandmother and her bread knife among them, so said their dad.</i> &lt;- There's the dehumanization and use of "they" - think "Save the Pearls" problematic attributions.<br /><br /><i>“No woman,” one of the men said to one of the others. “Wonder where she is?”<br /> “Oracle,” one of the others replied. “Not an easy one to catch.”<br /> “I know you speak our language,” Aoseh said, sterner this time. “Stop jabbering away like you don’t understand me."</i> Because you would have your darker skinned enemies speak a broken form of your prevalent language.<br /><br />Chapter 3: <i>“Today,” she told me, “is the first day that most Shotet will lay eyes on you, not to mention the rest of the galaxy. The last thing we want is for them to fixate on your hair. By fixing it up, we make it invisible. Understand?”<br /> I didn’t, but I didn’t press the issue. I was looking at my mother’s hair. It was dark, like mine, but a different texture—hers was so curly it trapped fingers, and mine was just straight enough to escape them.</i> My mouth dropped open at this inclusion because it's bad enough that people of color are often degraded by their natural hair types or forced to conform to some standard of beauty, and this serves to reinforce cultural self-hate of appearances in favor of the "majority" group's hair type. WTF man? <br /><br />Chapter 15: <i>“I’m not a fool, no matter what you people think of the Thuvhesit,” Akos snapped, his cheeks going ruddy as he picked up the practice blade. “You think I’m going to just let you set me up for a fall?”</i> &lt;- "You people" again. Dehumanizing language.<br /><br /><i>“So you, what? Leap straight to killing him? What is it with you Shotet?” Akos said in a low voice. </i> Akos says this to a Shotet person who makes a bargain with him, involving killing someone. Casual prejudicial assumptions even from the LI. Ugh. This is an offshoot of the same conversation in the mention above.<br /><br />There are a number of times when Cyra participates in her own self-hatred for identity, not just for what she's done and the secret she holds, but also her own ease of disposition for violence. This is contrasted against Akos, for when he subjects himself to a contract kill versus killing for survival, he's disgusted and nearly breaks down over the death. One could almost argue that in some ways Cyra corrupts him and he "fixes" her as his love interest, which I thought was pretty messed up in the context of the story.<br /><br />As far as the ableism goes, this book portrays such in two dimensions: chronic pain and self-harm/attributions to self-cutting. This narrative portrays the Shotet in demonizing way with respect to the novel's namesake "Carve the Mark". <br /><br />Chapter 15: <i>Akos rubbed at the marks by his elbow, and thought of the savagery of them.</i> Keep in mind this is a custom of the Shotet, and figures that he'd refer to it in some way as being "savage."<br /><br />The most damning quote I found was one I partially quoted in my status updates.<br /><br />Chapter 14: <i>"Says the person who’s been scarring herself for things she was coerced into doing,” he said wryly.<br /> It wasn’t funny, what either of us was saying. And then it was. I grinned, and after a moment, so did he. A new grin—not the one that told me he was proud of himself, or the one that he forced when he felt like he needed to be polite, but a thirsty, crazed kind of smile. </i> Basically the context of this is that Cyra was talking about how she marked herself not for the number of kills she made with her ability but for every time she had pain. I think this is triggering for people who may have recovered from some degree of self-harm/cutting. And the fact that Akos and Cyra laugh about it made me want to throw the book down in disgust, even if it is bitter/dark humor. It's not funny.<br /><br />And definitely not cool to romanticize chronic pain in the form of an attempted sacrifice:<br /><br />Chapter 25: <i>Akos’s eyes—full of tears, full of pain—found mine. Pushing the shadow toward him would have been easy. I had done it many times before, each time a mark on my left arm. All I had to do was let the connection form, let the pain pass between us like a breath, like a kiss. Let all of it flow out of me, bringing relief for us both, in death.<br /> But he did not deserve it.<br /> This time, I broke the connection, like slamming a door between us. I pulled the pain back, into myself, willing my body to grow darker and darker, like a bottle of pink. I shuddered with the force of that power, that agony.<br /> I didn’t scream. I wasn’t afraid. I knew I was strong enough to survive it all.</i><br /><br />I feel like there were more problems in this book than I could care to cite as far as the portrayals were concerned. I understood that this was supposed to be a narrative showcasing two very flawed characters put in extraordinary circumstances and brought together under those terms, but taking and appropriating from established cultures and loosely building a narrative with many haphazard stereotypes, some even affirming awful and harmful attributions, is really messed up. Romanticizing pain, including measures out of the control of the person suffering from it, isn't acceptable either.<br /><br />I definitely won't be reading the next book in this series. And I'm unlikely even to pick up another narrative by Roth in the future.<br /><br />Overall score: 1/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1892907818373398493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1709052487?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

          marked it as dnf


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008159481" href="/book/show/30233110-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1709052487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16953690689682757068"><b>DNF @ 22%</b> <br/>Sana and I are bored and are being put in a reading slump reading this. It's extremely slow and boring and nothing interesting has happened. We encountered some of the issues going on and asked each other if it was triggering for either of us and since it wasn't, we continued. I do agree that this does have issues that can be triggering for people, so I suggest watching out for that before starting it. We also have read like 2 more pages since our last update (pg. 108) and stopped ther</span>
  <span id="freeText16953690689682757068" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 22%</b> <br />Sana and I are bored and are being put in a reading slump reading this. It's extremely slow and boring and nothing interesting has happened. We encountered some of the issues going on and asked each other if it was triggering for either of us and since it wasn't, we continued. I do agree that this does have issues that can be triggering for people, so I suggest watching out for that before starting it. We also have read like 2 more pages since our last update (pg. 108) and stopped there. The book is just boring, overall, and I haven't been reading ever since. <br /><br />We tried, but the trying has to stop now. It's no surprise that this buddy read didn't work since it never works out for us. Sana I swear buddy reads don't like us.<br /><br /><b>3/3/17</b>: Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26402455-sana-khalid" rel="nofollow noopener">this evil child</a>. Like Sana, I'm either gonna hate this or love this because of the mixed reviews it has.<br /><br /><b>2/26/17</b>: I haven't read this book, but I was just looking at the reviews and so many readers have deleted their rating (only the rating) and added notes to the review saying this book deals with problematic issues that can be taken as offensive including ableism, racism, and disrespect. I still am gonna read this, but I'm not gonna write a review. I'll probably rate it, and I will look for the issues it has, but writing a review won't be necessary since it's already become a big problem.<br /><br />I don't know what it is, but there are some links here that talk about the book and give out some of the points on how this book has issues that people should look out for:<br /><br />- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://westwoodhorizon.com/11392/showcase/veronica-roths-carve-the-mark-unleashes-a-wave-of-controversy/">http://westwoodhorizon.com/11392/show...</a><br />- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://justinaireland.com/dammit-this-is-a-blog/2016/12/4/the-continent-carve-the-mark-and-the-trope-of-the-dark-skinned-aggressor">http://justinaireland.com/dammit-this...</a><br />- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.chicagotribune.com/lifestyles/books/ct-publishers-hiring-book-readers-to-flag-sensitivity-20170215-story.html">http://www.chicagotribune.com/lifesty...</a><br />- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://writtenwordworlds.wordpress.com/2016/12/30/carve-the-mark-book-review/">https://writtenwordworlds.wordpress.c...</a><br />- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://aragonoutlook.org/2017/02/roths-newest-novel-doesnt-hit-mark/">http://aragonoutlook.org/2017/02/roth...</a><br />- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://sabaatahir.tumblr.com/post/156055223595/how-can-you-support-veronica-roths-book-its">http://sabaatahir.tumblr.com/post/156...</a></span>

<div id="review_1848458863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1848458863" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1848458863?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008159481" href="/book/show/30233110-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1848458863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14448000264607134479"><b>EDIT 11/02/2017/</b>: Lowering my rating to two stars because holy moley, I already don't remember a thing of what happened in this book. And I read it, like, a month ago. This is <i>Lady Midnight</i> happening to me all over again. Is it my memory's fault or these run-of-the-mill-yet-super-popular books'?<br/><br/>---<br/><br/><b>“Growing up here really has warped you, hasn’t it?”<br/>“Growing up here,” I clarified, “has made me see the truth about people.”</b><br/><br/>•I feel that <b>a foreword</b> is needed here. <br/><b>First</b>, I read the Divergent trilogy a</span>
  <span id="freeText14448000264607134479" style="display:none"><b>EDIT 11/02/2017/</b>: Lowering my rating to two stars because holy moley, I already don't remember a thing of what happened in this book. And I read it, like, a month ago. This is <i>Lady Midnight</i> happening to me all over again. Is it my memory's fault or these run-of-the-mill-yet-super-popular books'?<br /><br />---<br /><br /><b>“Growing up here really has warped you, hasn’t it?”<br />“Growing up here,” I clarified, “has made me see the truth about people.”</b><br /><br />•I feel that <b>a foreword</b> is needed here. <br /><b>First</b>, I read the Divergent trilogy a little over two years ago, before the first movie -the only one I watched- was released, and the series as a whole impressed me so little I reckon my mind let my memories of it fade by default. So if what you need is a detailed comparison between the Divergent series and <i>Carve the Mark</i>, this is not the review you're looking for. <br /><b>Secondly</b>, I feel duty-bound to let you know that <b><i>Carve the Mark</i> has raised <a href="http://justinaireland.com/dammit-this-is-a-blog/2016/12/4/the-continent-carve-the-mark-and-the-trope-of-the-dark-skinned-aggressor" rel="nofollow noopener">issues</a></b> regarding racism and cultural stereotypes and the author's thoughts about chronic illnesses -also with reference to <a href="http://www.npr.org/templates/transcript/transcript.php?storyId=509650409&amp;ft=nprml&amp;f=509650409" rel="nofollow noopener">this interview</a>. Here I won't comment on the substance of the matter; I'll only say that before starting the book, I had no idea of the uproar surrounding it, and that I didn't find out until later, when I was almost done with it. Which means, yes, that I picked up none of these issues while reading, but then again, I am white and I have no first-hand experience of what it means to cope with a chronic condition, so I do not fall into that category of people who are likely to be touched by them. I feel like it's not my place to pass judgement on this; so<b> please do not be offended by my not-totally-negative opinion of the book</b>. I mean no disrespect whatsoever, I am glad that the problem has been duly pointed out and I'm sorry for all the readers who may have been hurt by this.<br /><br />•Strangely enough, when it comes to this novel I seem to be more inclined to dwell on the things I <i>won't</i> talk about than on those few points I could actually wring something out of. First things first, then: I was deeply fascinated with <b>the concept</b> lying at the basis of this world-building, namely, this unspecified current that flows across the whole universe, and to which the gifts, special powers that manifest differently for each individual, are due. The explanation of this phenomenon is that since each person is unique, when the energy of the current fills them, it takes different shapes, and hence the difference in the powers. I found this idea very simple, yet very <b>suggestive</b>, and <b>logically convincing</b> too, which is never to be undervalued.<br /><br />•Sadly, this single fact was the only thing that genuinely struck me as original and truly thought-out. The rest of <b>the world building</b> was to me not bad, but rather dull and <b>unsurprising</b>, and <b>not perfectly laid out</b> if we're being honest. In this world, many -some? Anyway, more than one- planets are inhabited by humans, but I couldn't gather exactly how many and why; plus, the names of these planets and their peoples are mentioned more than once along with inconsequential facts like, for instance, that Ogra culture worships mystery (what does that even <i>mean</i>, for goodness sake) but that doesn't help you getting a clearer picture <i>at all</i>. <b>It basically fills up your mind with random names you're bound to forget once the paragraph is over</b>. <br /><br />•<b>The pace</b> -good gracious, the pace. It's no secret that Veronica Roth never really knew what to do with this alien thing, and the obvious result is, I got bored with <i>Insurgent</i>, I got bored with <i>Allegiant</i>, and <b>I got bored </b>with <i>Carve the Mark</i>. (I believe <i>Divergent</i> is exempted simply because back then Roth was still too inexperienced a writer to realize that the pace is something you need to pay attention to; see the irony in this?) The first part, more introductory, was made interesting by the novelty of the world and of the characters, but <b>the second part is really tough to get through</b>. <b>The writing</b>, being not particularly brilliant and, again, simply <b>average</b>, doesn't help much; the same applies to <b>the plot</b>.<br /> <br />•In spite of everything I said so far, I found <b>the main characters</b>, Cyra and Akos, to be <b>compelling enough</b>, which definitely helped in making it to the end of the book. Ad for the rest of the cast, well, I liked the villain, but apart from these three, no one else is worth special mention.<br /><br />➽ Since that little yet so charming detail in the world-building won me over so thoroughly, and since I am genuinely curious to know how some of the dynamics established between some of the characters will play out, <b>I will be picking the sequel up</b>. I didn't love it, but if what you're looking for is a world for you to flee to, a story for you to relax with, then <i>Carve the Mark</i> is as good any.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14448000264607134479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1823504762" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1823504762" />
    <a title="Frankie Lovely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely"><img alt="Frankie Lovely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493240668p2/61971658.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1823504762?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frankie Lovely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frankie Lovely" href="/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely">Frankie Lovely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=2017-release">2017-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=hyped">hyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=read-it-in-2017">read-it-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=controversy">controversy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1823504762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13924463449353308610"><b>2 stars</b><br/><b>Uncensored review</b> as always<br/>And <b>spoiler-free</b><br/><br/>Oh boy. <u>This is not going to be pretty</u>. I’m sure you have seen all the upchucked Haterade that the “controversy brigade” so generously spewed about this book before and after it’s release. So obviously, I wanted to love this book SO HARD if only to shove a raving review in the face of absurdity! Unfortunately, I can’t do that here.<br/><br/>*sulks*<br/><br/>On the other hand … I honestly did not see ANY of the controversy. Like … where is it? I have no idea. I’m sur</span>
  <span id="freeText13924463449353308610" style="display:none"><b>2 stars</b><br /><b>Uncensored review</b> as always<br />And <b>spoiler-free</b><br /><br />Oh boy. <u>This is not going to be pretty</u>. I’m sure you have seen all the upchucked Haterade that the “controversy brigade” so generously spewed about this book before and after it’s release. So obviously, I wanted to love this book SO HARD if only to shove a raving review in the face of absurdity! Unfortunately, I can’t do that here.<br /><br />*sulks*<br /><br />On the other hand … I honestly did not see ANY of the controversy. Like … where is it? I have no idea. I’m sure some “helpful” person will take the time to “enlighten” me in the comments below (hint: don’t. Because I honestly don't care). Sadly, large portions of this book were just confusing and slow. But we will start with the positives … because I’m not a <i>complete</i> asshole.<br /><br /><b>What I did like</b><br /><br />The best part of this book (for me) was all the culture building Roth so intricately weaved together for this world. Some of you may find this part a bit info-dumpy … but I'm a total nerd for stuff like this so I loved it! All the fascinating religious beliefs, languages, history. Yeah … totally my jam and I ate it with a spoon and a smile. These are the things that shape a society. These are the things that create diversity, discrimination, conflict and war! These are the things that help to shape an individual (along with personal experience and learned/inherited behavior). Which brings me to another thing I loved about this book.<br /><br />Roth did an incredible job building her characters from a psychological standpoint. Personal histories were laid beautifully throughout this book, making the characters intricate and intriguing and real. People are not black or white, good or bad. People are tapestries of gray with shades of every manner of influence woven through. All broken, all healing, all scared and walled and pieced in varying ways.<br /><br />I could continue on this subject for a while, inevitably meandering into a major psychology lecture the likes of which we many never escape … so I shall move along. But before I dive headfirst into negativity land … I want to acknowledge the fact that, while I will not take the time to chronicle each and every moment/plot-point/collection-of-words that I liked about this book, I did enjoy the story for the most part. It truly is a good concept and story, and with a good pair of scissors in the hand of a less forgiving editor, this would have been a much more successful read.<br /><br /><b>What I did <i>not</i> like</b><br /><br />What the fuck is going on? <br />Where are we? <br />What the hell is this place? <br />How did we get here? <br />What color are the walls?<br /><br />This is an example of the types of questions I may have asked myself while stumbling through this book. Let's face it, the descriptions of actual places were basically non-existent. I like to fancy myself as having a pretty active imagination, but even I had major trouble visualizing scenes while reading this. Honestly, the beginning of this book really roped me in (I quite enjoyed a good portion of the first part of this book). Unfortunately, the middle dropped all form entirely and became a cluster fuck of what-the-fucks … and it didn’t get any better from there. To add to the utter confusion ... I often felt like I was missing huge chunks of time. Like ... we were here ... then all the sudden we’re over there ... and I had no idea why or how. <br /><br />To say that a majority of this book was confusing as fuck would be an appropriate assessment. Confusing and slooooooow (and I don't mind slow but this was not a good slow). Honestly this was really my biggest and perhaps only complaint with this book. As I mentioned above, the concept and the story was actually quite decent. But when you can’t focus because you are either confused or bored … a great concept really fails to hold sway. The point of fiction is to transfer your reader to another time/place/world. But in order for that to be effective, the world first has to be built. This was the utter failing of this book and unfortunately, it’s a doozy. <br /><br /><b>In Conclusion</b><br />Great concept. Good plot. Poor execution. Slow and confusing. I would not recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13924463449353308610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
