<div id="review_1877231362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1877231362" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1877231362?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2017-releases">2017-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1877231362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7275083775854563519">I liked the story overall! But there a few things that might <i>seem</i> minor, but are actually really detracting from the story, and I took issue with them. It was a good story, don't get me wrong. But I have some things to explore in my review that I just didn't like.<br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2017/01/review-carve-mark-by-veronica-roth.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Carve the Mark by Veronica Roth<br/>Book One of the Carve the Mark series<br/>Publisher: Katherine Tegen Books<br/>Publication Date: January 17, 2017<br/>Rating: 3 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary</span>
  <span id="freeText7275083775854563519" style="display:none">I liked the story overall! But there a few things that might <i>seem</i> minor, but are actually really detracting from the story, and I took issue with them. It was a good story, don't get me wrong. But I have some things to explore in my review that I just didn't like.<br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2017/01/review-carve-mark-by-veronica-roth.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Carve the Mark by Veronica Roth<br />Book One of the Carve the Mark series<br />Publisher: Katherine Tegen Books<br />Publication Date: January 17, 2017<br />Rating: 3 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />On a planet where violence and vengeance rule, in a galaxy where some are favored by fate, everyone develops a currentgift, a unique power meant to shape the future. While most benefit from their currentgifts, Akos and Cyra do not—their gifts make them vulnerable to others’ control. Can they reclaim their gifts, their fates, and their lives, and reset the balance of power in this world?<br /><br />Cyra is the sister of the brutal tyrant who rules the Shotet people. Cyra’s currentgift gives her pain and power—something her brother exploits, using her to torture his enemies. But Cyra is much more than just a blade in her brother’s hand: she is resilient, quick on her feet, and smarter than he knows.<br /><br />Akos is from the peace-loving nation of Thuvhe, and his loyalty to his family is limitless. Though protected by his unusual currentgift, once Akos and his brother are captured by enemy Shotet soldiers, Akos is desperate to get his brother out alive—no matter what the cost. When Akos is thrust into Cyra’s world, the enmity between their countries and families seems insurmountable. They must decide to help each other to survive—or to destroy one another.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />Carve the Mark is absolutely worth the hype and the excitement, and it's definitely worth your time to read this book if you've been looking forward to reading it. Chances are, it won't disappoint you. In many ways, I liked this book a lot. But there were several specific things that might seem small or insignificant in the grand schemes of things, that ended up really bothering me. Hence, the three-star rating. <br /><br />This story is told by two characters - Akos, a Thuvhe, and Cyra, a Shotet. The Thuvhe are a peace-loving people living on Urek. The Shotet are more aggressive nomadic people that conquer various nations and planets. When he is fourteen, Akos is captured, along with his brother, by the Shotet, who kill his father in front of him. They are taken to the Shotet stronghold of Urek, ruled by Ryzek Noavek, a ruthless tyrant and older brother of Cyra. They are stolen for their currentgifts - Akos's brother Eijeh is the next oracle of the Thuvhe. Akos grows into his currentgift - he can interrupt the current (he can cancel it out, turn it off, that sort of thing). Several years later, Akos is shaped into a warrior, but he has lost known of his humanity. He is not a killer, though he has killed to protect himself. He is brought to help Cyra Noavek, whose currentgift is inflicting pain on others with her touch. No one can touch her without feeling pain, but Akos can, because he interrupts the current (and all currentgifts are "fueled" by the current). Akos cooperates because he wants to rescue his brother and flee. But the more he and Cyra interact, the more they learn about each other, and the more they realize that they share common interests, interests that could incite wars.<br /><br />The beginning of the book was incredibly confusing (I'll talk about that in the next section), but once I (sort of) got a grasp of the world and everything going on, I started to get into the story and really sink into it. This is science fiction, though certain elements (like the currentgifts) can definitely be categorized as fantasy. This story takes place across planets of a galaxy, so it's a space-y type of science fiction. <br /><br />I must say, Roth did an excellent job with the characterization and character growth, specifically in terms of Cyra and Akos. I'll start with Akos. He is easily my favorite character of the book. He is Thuvhe, and so he is brought up to be more peaceful and somewhat passive towards violence. Even several years being trained as a Shotet soldier doesn't break him down. He is compassionate, and he is strong. I liked him a lot, especially for his unbreakable will. I was amazing and in awe of how much pain and grief and despair he bore, for years. Akos grows into a character that still hates killing, and is sick over having to kill anyone, but can do it. He becomes so strong and capable in other ways, and he's also extremely intelligent and clever. He isn't an alpha type of YA hero - he's quietly intelligent and very, very human. <br /><br />Cyra is almost the opposite of him, yet it slowly becomes apparent that she has similarities to him. She appears to be a brutal, cold, emotionless killer summoned and used by her brother, Ryzek. But Cyra does not enjoy wielding her painful power over others, and she definitely does not enjoy bending to Ryzek's will. In many ways, it is Akos who shows her mercy, what mercy is, and that she is still capable of being merciful, and better, and more. Cyra learns to turn her pain into something else. She loses none of her deadliness and her danger, but as the story goes on, she becomes stronger and more able to stand up to Ryzek.<br /><br />Once I got past the first one hundred pages or so, I had little difficulty getting through the story. I was pretty engrossed and despite the book being rather long, I read it quickly. There is so much happening in this story, and I wanted to see how it would all end. There were so many moments when things could go disastrously wrong, and I held my breath as I turned the pages. No one can say that certain parts of this book weren't engrossing. A lot of the story ends up being about how to unseat Ryzek, and how to stay alive and protect each other.<br /><br />There is romance! I liked seeing Akos and Cyra fall for each other. It's actually Cyra who shows her feelings first, which you wouldn't expect. Cyra is supposedly the more ruthless one, and Akos is the more emotional and merciful one. But it's Cyra that starts to fall for Akos first, and shows her hand first. I liked their dynamic a lot - they learn to trust each other before anything else. No love triangle! Thank goodness for that. I thought this romance was well-developed, and swoony towards the end.<br /><br />There is also another romance which I thought was sweet. I can't say much about it because it'll spoil things, but it's between two characters that are good together. <br /><br />The ending, as insane and chaotic as it is, is not a cruel ending. There is no horrible cliffhanger, which is surprising, since this is book one of a duology. You'd expect something really terrible to have happened at the end, hurting the main character(s). Don't get me wrong, terrible (permanent) things definitely happened; but the ending isn't a cliffhanger, and I definitely appreciate that.<br /><br />Now I'm going to talk about the things I didn't really enjoy. <br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />First: the initial one hundred pages or so? Very confusing, and very boring too. I had a hard time getting through the beginning of the story. There is so much information dumped into the first couple of chapters, and so many names. It also took me a while to realize that the beginning is when Akos is fourteen - and NOT the "present" time of the story. Same with Cyra's beginning - she is six when her chapter begins. The beginning has too much going on, and it isn't well-explained at first. I had to reread several of the chapters a few times to really get some sort of grasp as to what was happening.<br /><br />I'm not sure I really understand the world/world-building? Currentgifts and their origin and how/why they exist still kind of elude me. What is the "current"? Where did it come from? How is it magically given people these currentgifts? The currentgifts are things like inflicting pain upon touch, or not feeling pain at all, or seeing the future, or seeing every memory of a person. <br /><br />Second: there are so many awful, brutal scenes in this book. I'm talking about torture and cruel treatment of people. I understand that this type of brutality is very real and exists in real life and has a place in this fictional world, but the brutality of a lot of it... didn't sit well with me. Usually a certain level of violence doesn't bother me too much? The violence in this book, while not exactly graphic, is horrifying. Which is probably the intent, but my stomach hurt, reading it. <br /><br />Third: Not the biggest thing I didn't like, but I wasn't a huge fan of having Akos's POV in third-person, and then Cyra's in first-person. I loved reading from both of their POVs! But it would have been nice to have a little uniformity (either both in first, or both in third). Also it already scares me, that Roth chooses to tell this story from both Akos and Cyra's POVs. We saw what happened in Allegiant...<br /><br />Fourth: problematic racial content. Oh yeah, I definitely see where people are coming from, when they say that this book has some racist content. The Shotet are portrayed as "brown skinned", aggressive, nomadic people. They stole Thuvhe children years ago, and the Thuvhe retaliated and stole Shotet children, but the way the story is told, the Shotet are the "villains". I mean, given that the first chapter is about Akos's father getting brutally murdered in front of him, I get why that would be implication. But there are definitely underlying tones of something problematic here: the Thuvhe, light-skinned peaceful people, and the Shotet, darker-skinned aggressive people, are both cliches. And what's more, it seems like most of the Shotet have very violent currentgifts, whereas the Thuvhe have more passive, non-violent gifts (like Akos's, or his mother's, or his brother's). <br /><br />Do you see the problem here? Why is it that the "aggressive" people are always the brown/darker-skinned ones, and the more "peaceful" non-violent people are lighter-skinned? I have no qualms with the characters themselves (I adore Akos, and Cyra is such a fighter), but the social construct here is reflective of cliches and stereotypes. <br /><br />Read THIS peace if you want more information. I definitely do not know it all, but I recognize and understand the issue at hand here, in terms of race and culture.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />Yes, I had issues with this book, and I firmly believe that last issue needs to be addressed. And yes, I also enjoyed the book, for the most part, regardless. It's a good story, and I was definitely swept up in the story as I was reading. I'll be reading the sequel next year. I don't know if I really should recommend this book, given the evident issues. But I did like the story too. If you've been excited to read this book, believe me, it probably won't disappoint. But... recognize issues when you see them. Talk about them. Discuss and learn.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />3 stars. Like I said, this is a good story, and of all of Roth's books, it's probably her best. I think I liked it more than I liked her other books (definitely more than I liked Insurgent and Allegiant - though I never fully read Allegiant). I want to see where the story goes. But there were some things that held me back a little, in terms of my rating. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7275083775854563519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer3685025579639491653">I refuse to put myself in a position where the likelihood of myself being triggered is high. I don't think the "kill marks" which feature in this book are okay. My friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1782320836' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cait</a> talks more about how they these marks can be connected to self harm. I was curious about this book but after hearing several quotes which feature in the book about these marks I am physically sick and disgusted. It honestly saddens me. I wonder how such a thing passed by so many ARC readers though. <br/><br/>The cover itself is a re</span>
  <span id="freeText3685025579639491653" style="display:none">I refuse to put myself in a position where the likelihood of myself being triggered is high. I don't think the "kill marks" which feature in this book are okay. My friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1782320836" rel="nofollow noopener">Cait</a> talks more about how they these marks can be connected to self harm. I was curious about this book but after hearing several quotes which feature in the book about these marks I am physically sick and disgusted. It honestly saddens me. I wonder how such a thing passed by so many ARC readers though. <br /><br />The cover itself is a representation of self harm. Something that people also need to be aware of. It is not simply a wall with gold paint. <br /><br />Please proceed with caution if you choose to read this book despite the triggers present. Stay safe. As soon as you feel even slightly triggered, put the book down. Your mental health and physical well being is more important than this story. Please be careful, you're all too important.<br /><br />On top of all this, there are racist stereotypes and ableist attitudes all throughout this book. Something which shouldn't be supported at all, in my opinion. <br /><br />Also, to tell people their opinion about the racism, ableism and triggers which feature in this book is invalid or wrong is highly ignorant behaviour . You are allowed to enjoy this book, but stay away of the problems that do feature and stay open to others opinions, especially those who have been harmed by this novel.<br /><br />For more information on the ableism, which is primarily about chronic pain because described as a gift, read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834915407?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Emer's</a> review. She suffers from chronic pain and talks about her views on the topic. </span>

<div id="review_1897994904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1897994904" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1897994904?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=boooring">boooring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=derp-moments">derp-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dragged-on-too-much">dragged-on-too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=lgbtqia-if-you-squint">lgbtqia-if-you-squint</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=typical">typical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=when-sparks-don-t-fly">when-sparks-don-t-fly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=the-earth-is-flat">the-earth-is-flat</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=mommy-why-is-the-villain-bad">mommy-why-is-the-villain-bad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897994904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12454350022129412630"><blockquote>
  <i>"I didn't choose the blood that runs in my veins," I replied. "Any more than you chose your fate. You and I, we've become what we were made to become."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I feel like I could throw a dart in a bookstore and hit at least a dozen YA books with practically the same quote and premise. <br/><br/>The nature vs nurture debate is well-trodden ground in fiction, not just in YA. Is there such thing as fate? Are villains born or made? These are all themes that can be reinvigorated and made fresh and unique, but <b>Carv</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12454350022129412630" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"I didn't choose the blood that runs in my veins," I replied. "Any more than you chose your fate. You and I, we've become what we were made to become."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I feel like I could throw a dart in a bookstore and hit at least a dozen YA books with practically the same quote and premise. <br><br>The nature vs nurture debate is well-trodden ground in fiction, not just in YA. Is there such thing as fate? Are villains born or made? These are all themes that can be reinvigorated and made fresh and unique, but <b>Carve The Mark just fails across the board.</b><br><br>I'm the first to admit <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a> had its problems. But at least it was fun, fast-paced, and filled a Harry Potter and the Hunger Games niche. Carve The Mark is boring. Lifeless. Take them out of space and it'd be a more standard dystopian than its comparison title Divergent. And it ends abruptly just when things are getting exciting, as though it knows it needs something to bring readers back.<br><br>There's absolutely nothing noteworthy about the main characters Cyra and Akos. They're just <i>there</i>, taking up space, saying their lines, running through the motions. It's a mark of how utterly blah they are that <b>their banter falls flat.</b> Not a single crooked grin graced my mouth while reading.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461890067ra/18926548.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The <b>romance is formulaic</b> and didn't carry as much depth as it should have. Akos was captured by Cyra's people (the Shotet) as a child. Her brother ordered the murder of his father and brother. He is a prisoner falling in love with his captor, but he spends a weirdly short amount of time analyzing this.<br><br>Where's the self-loathing? I can't believe I'm asking this, but <b>where's the angst?</b> He accepts his feelings far too easily for someone in his position. <br><br>I personally think Ryzek, Cyra's power-hungry brother, is a far more interesting character to focus on because his currentgift allows him to swap out his own memories for someone else's. It explores the question of how much your past defines your personality. The person usually on the receiving end of these memory swaps is Akos's brother Elijah. Unfortunately, Roth insists on shining the spotlight on the boring siblings. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488966337ra/22172320.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finally, the <b>chronic pain/self-harm glorification</b>:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"The gift," I said, "is the strength the curse has given me." The new answer was a blooming hushflower, petals unfurling. "I can bear it. I can bear pain. I can bear anything."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>For the record, the title refers to a Shotet practice where lines are carved on their arm to mark their kills. Pain is a main theme in Carve the Mark and is ultimately presented as something positive, something that helps you build character. <br><br>There has been considerable outrage over this, which you can Google. While I agree that this message has some uncomfortable implications, I sort of understand why Roth wrote it the way she did. Her religious beliefs, I personally think, shape the way she writes. It's why she ended <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18710190.Allegiant__Divergent___3_" title="Allegiant (Divergent, #3) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Allegiant</a> the way <a href="http://veronicarothbooks.blogspot.hk/2013/10/about-end-of-allegiant-spoilers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">she did</a>. <br><br>(Please note that this is pure speculation and I could be as wrong as BBC Sherlock fans who thought Mary Watson was working for Moriarty. But the English major in me won't shut up.)<br><br>Overall, I expected <i>more</i>. More from YA, more from an author who has an international bestseller and a film franchise under her belt. <br><br>I won't be waiting for the sequel with baited breath.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12454350022129412630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17976684793245319304"><b>4.75 Golden stars!</b><br/><br/>wow! I didn't think I would love this story this much! the characters, the thrills, this beautiful world!<br/>Splendid!<br/>To be honest I didn't even expect it to be a space sci-fi, & it was wonderful!<br/>I was looking for a satisfying sensible Space sci-fi & this book mostly met my expectations! I really enjoyed it.<br/>---<br/>World Building: ★★★★★/5<br/>the world, the usual jobs, every responsibilities, the rules & the gifts. everything was great! it took its times to get used to this totally-new world</span>
  <span id="freeText17976684793245319304" style="display:none"><b>4.75 Golden stars!</b><br /><br />wow! I didn't think I would love this story this much! the characters, the thrills, this beautiful world!<br />Splendid!<br />To be honest I didn't even expect it to be a space sci-fi, &amp; it was wonderful!<br />I was looking for a satisfying sensible Space sci-fi &amp; this book mostly met my expectations! I really enjoyed it.<br />---<br />World Building: ★★★★★/5<br />the world, the usual jobs, every responsibilities, the rules &amp; the gifts. everything was great! it took its times to get used to this totally-new world &amp; their new made-up words in measuring times. but it is awesome, if you love sci-fi.<br />-<br />Characters: ★★★★★/5<br />I already said, I loved Akos. he was strong, vulnerable, caring &amp; sensitive... he was one of my sweathearts. at some parts he made me laugh.<br />Cyra wasn't added to my few favourite female characters, but she was actually good &amp; not annoying. she was caring &amp; thoughtful &amp; strong. (that means she wasn't added to my hated female protagonists either.) I liked her &amp; how she acted.<br />also villains' behavior made very much sense &amp; they were well-created, well-written<br /><br />Characters developments: ★★★★★/5<br />-<br />Love life: ★★★★/5<br />I have a ship or maybe two. enough amount of love life that attracts readers to love their relationships (especially a person like me who don't like detailed love relationship descriptions, or I don't care if there isn't many love moments)<br />-<br />Plot: ★★★★(★)/5<br />Everything goes perfectly awesome &amp; at some parts, the things went on as I wished. at some parts it went downhill, but every books has its up (adrenaline) &amp; down (valleys between the events) I clutched the edge of my seat in the end! I loved it.<br />-<br />general idea: ★★★★★/5<br />the general idea behind the story was so unique &amp; I loved it. it was in space, but not all happening in space-ships like some space sci-fi, I reminded without thinking by default. it was a wholly new solar system with advanced technology &amp; societies.<br />at some little parts it reminded me of 'Red queen' &amp; 'Keeper of the universe'. I didn't much enjoy red queen because I didn't like the protagonist. but I loved this one, as I like both. plus in this story is no maid &amp; help-me-what-I-am-supposed-to-wear vibes (I've read enough of that!) it was more like a Dark big castle for a cruel kingdom.<br />-<br />Writing style: ★★★★/5<br />enough amounts of Adrenaline events, love emotions, feelings, fiction, humor &amp; descriptions. :)<br />tho everyone said it had slow pace but I read it in 2 days &amp; for me the plot &amp; the world was so interesting &amp; intriguing, I couldn't put it down, so it was a quick read for me.<br />......<br />that's it.<br />hope it is helpful &amp; you will enjoy reading the book as much as I did.</span>

<div id="review_2051258158" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2051258158" />
    <a title="Francina Simone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3605877-francina-simone"><img alt="Francina Simone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590534102p2/3605877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2051258158?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Francina Simone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Francina Simone" href="/user/show/3605877-francina-simone">Francina Simone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30133224-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2051258158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16899519315820601573">Ok...I'm gonna film a review tomorrow and talk about something. Over al, objectively, I'm bouncing between 4-4.5 more towards a 4. Subjectively...really not my style so more of a 3 if you have similar "preferences" as me.<br/><br/>As far as everything else goes, I'll get a video up soon to discuss all my thoughts 😉</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1890406261" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890406261" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1890406261?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30182503-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=as">as</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1890406261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1008168366340604528">This was a YA sci-fi/fantasy story, set in a different universe.<br/><br/>I liked how strong Akos was in this story, and he really did hold up under some terrible circumstances. I also liked Cyra, who put up with so much pain from such a young age, and was still able to be feared, and able to stand up to her brother when she needed to.<br/><br/>The world building in this was pretty good, although it did take quite a while for it all to come out, and the odd-sounding names did make things a little more difficult. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText1008168366340604528" style="display:none">This was a YA sci-fi/fantasy story, set in a different universe.<br><br>I liked how strong Akos was in this story, and he really did hold up under some terrible circumstances. I also liked Cyra, who put up with so much pain from such a young age, and was still able to be feared, and able to stand up to her brother when she needed to.<br><br>The world building in this was pretty good, although it did take quite a while for it all to come out, and the odd-sounding names did make things a little more difficult. The storyline was also good, and we had Akos and his elder brother being kidnapped by Cyra’s older brother Ryzek, both because of their ‘fates’, and because of their ‘currentgifts’. The pace in this was quite slow though, and it did take me a long time to get through it, but the story was enjoyable overall.<br><br>The ending to this was good, and it will be interesting to see what happens in the next book of the series.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433066772i/15045457.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>7 out of 10</span>
  <a data-text-id="1008168366340604528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1882994792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1882994792" />
    <a title="Ceilidh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh"><img alt="Ceilidh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422140120p2/3229028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1882994792?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceilidh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceilidh" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh">Ceilidh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30182503-carve-the-mark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1882994792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6156432778685993906">"Carve The Mark is straining to be everything to everyone yet ends up hollow and soulless. It is a novel seemingly comprised of editorial requests yet seems to have been untouched by the editing process. It begs to be unique in its world-building but falls so fast into the most derivative of tropes that parts feel like straight-up copying. It is devoid of any display of technical competence, with clumsy plotting, soporific pacing that only wakes up when it remembers it’s got a sequel coming, per</span>
  <span id="freeText6156432778685993906" style="display:none">"Carve The Mark is straining to be everything to everyone yet ends up hollow and soulless. It is a novel seemingly comprised of editorial requests yet seems to have been untouched by the editing process. It begs to be unique in its world-building but falls so fast into the most derivative of tropes that parts feel like straight-up copying. It is devoid of any display of technical competence, with clumsy plotting, soporific pacing that only wakes up when it remembers it’s got a sequel coming, perfunctory characterization of an ensemble witnessed in countless sci-fi knock-offs, and dueling narrations nearly identical in style with nothing to separate them. It is staggering to this reader that such a hotly hyped work by an author who has sold over 35m books was allowed to leave the printers in this pathetic state. Being a well written book would not undo the real harm it does in its portrayal of the race and illness issues, but the ineptitude surrounding that only heightens the sheer size of the mess. Popularity does not instantly equate quality, but to see a work surrounded by such anticipation that is lacking in the simplest display of competence is confusing and just a little bit sad."<br /><br />Read the full review at Bibliodaze. Spoilers within.<br /><br />I hated this book.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bibliodaze.com/2017/01/review-carve-the-mark-by-veronica-roth/">http://bibliodaze.com/2017/01/review-...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6156432778685993906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4mYsO9DHxbKEPiVsVARxtnLynbz2cl/EPylufyeqrGiciCRJ1rba5jToHxZFD/EB3KTpKKoezsVrlmCFxNOy8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ErGtSpVX+yFXkFtW2EwW2moRniF4YNZ2tKMtzRFE3zVsX6U4kybkdedGYSzJR5ZtxEfqtSQMR3fgHCM38j3BrQ==')})
  }
